Local News

Yesterday's Memorial Meeting for the Zhaoh He Ship Uprising - City Party Headquarters, Seamen's Party Headquarters, Seamen's Union, Zhaoh He School, and Others Held Meetings to Commemorate

Yesterday was the 18th anniversary of the Zhaoh He warship uprising. The City Party Headquarters specially convened representatives from all walks of life in the city at 9 AM yesterday morning at the auditorium on the third floor to hold a memorial meeting. A large number of people attended.

Venue Decoration

The city party headquarters was decorated with the Party flag and a white cloth banner which read "Shanghai representatives from all walks of life hold memorial meeting for the 18th anniversary of the Zhaoh He warship uprising," over the entrance. In the center of the auditorium hung a portrait of the Premier, flanked by the Party flag and slogans maintaining order. The walls were covered with slogans, creating a solemn atmosphere.

Attendees

Huang Zaoxiong from the City Party Headquarters, Lin Xiangyuan from the Hai Rong warship, Gao Rufeng from the Ning Hai warship, Feng Baozhen from the City Land Bureau, Ma Jiazhen from the City Education Association, Wang Longzhang from the City Cooperative Enterprise Promotion Association, Zhu Yakui from the Labor Education Committee, Mao Yun from the Second Special District Citizens' Association, He Yuanming from the Accountants' Association, Fu Changyu from the Grain Association, Hu Xiongding from Jiaotong University, Xu Shushen from He'an Elementary School, Huang Shihua from Wanzhu Elementary School, Yao Yongbo from Huiqiao Elementary School, Ju Fudan from Meixi Elementary School, and more than two hundred representatives from various agencies, organizations, schools, and party branches at all levels.

Meeting Staff

Chairman: Huang Zaoxiong; Recorder: Du Mengsen; Master of Ceremonies: Ye Guanqian; Reception: Huang Xianggu, Tong Muge, Li Erbai, Fan Mingyao, Lai Zhiwen, Zhang Hanyun, Zhu Xiaochun, Lin Keqiang, Cao Runsen, Wang Guoping, Bao Huizhong, etc. Armed police officers from the Third Squadron of the Police Brigade maintained order at the venue and guarded the area near the City Party Headquarters.

Meeting Order

(1) Opening of the meeting; (2) Singing the Party song; (3) Bowing to the Party flag and the portrait of the Premier; (4) Reading the Premier's will; (5) Silence; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Speeches; (8) Shouting slogans; (9) Adjournment.

Chairman's Report

After performing the formalities, Chairman Huang Zaoxiong gave a report, stating that today is the anniversary of the Zhaoh He warship uprising. The meaning of this commemoration and the circumstances of its passage are explained in detail in the publicity outline and need not be repeated. There are two points worth noting in this commemoration: (1) This commemoration can be said to be the commemoration of the recreation of the Republic of China. Since the Xinhai Revolution, people generally believed that the revolution had succeeded. Therefore, revolutionary thought gradually declined, and revolutionaries became increasingly corrupt. Yuan Shikai took the opportunity to seize power and expand his influence to the south, oppressing party members and plotting to restore the imperial system. Seeing this phenomenon, the Premier actively sought another countermeasure. At that time, Chen Ying Shi, a martyr, was ordered to work in Shanghai, which led to the Zhaoh He uprising. This action is most valuable to the history of our party. This is the first point. (2) There are many revolutionary anniversaries, but this anniversary is even more worthy of commemoration. At that time, Yuan's party was all over the place. The martyrs Wang Xiaofeng and Wang Mingshan assassinated Zheng Rucheng at the Baidu Bridge, surrendered generously, and died calmly. This kind of behavior of killing oneself to achieve benevolence is rarely seen at present, and so on.

Representative Speeches

After the chairman's report, Xu Shushen, the principal of He'an Elementary School, gave a speech, stating that the significance of the Zhaoh He warship uprising anniversary is to eliminate the hidden reefs of our party's destiny. Premier Sun led our party. If there were no hidden reefs before, the revolution would not have succeeded until the Xinhai Revolution. Since the initial success of the Xinhai Revolution, the Chinese people believed that it would shine brightly. Unexpectedly, they encountered a major hidden reef, that is, Yuan Shikai's brewing of the imperial system. At that time, Yuan Shikai outwardly obeyed the party's orders and secretly plotted for autocracy. Chen Ying Shi and others launched an uprising in Shanghai. Unfortunately, at that time, the Chinese people's minds were old and numb, so the Zhaoh He warship still could not succeed. The reason was the lack of publicity. The impact of the Zhaoh He uprising later broke Yuan Shikai's dream of being an emperor. But how many hidden reefs are there? Such as Zhang Xun's restoration, warlord infighting, and the people have no peace. Even now, they cannot be completely eliminated. The biggest hidden reefs at present are the internal harassment of the Communist bandits and the external oppression of imperialism. This has caused obstacles to the revolutionary cause everywhere, and construction events cannot proceed smoothly. Facing these obstacles, it is all because the Chinese people have different steps and different opinions, and they fight each other, resulting in the current situation. Today's commemoration of Zhaoh He, we should unify the psychology of each individual from this point, enrich the strength and ideas of our compatriots and comrades, and strive to revive and build a new Republic of China.

Slogans

(1) The Zhaoh He uprising was a revolutionary feat to support the Republic of China and overthrow the imperial system; (2) The Zhaoh He uprising was a major key to the revival of the Republic of China; (3) The Zhaoh He uprising was the prelude to the successful uprising in Yunnan; (4) Commemorating the Zhaoh He uprising, we must prepare to recover the four northeastern provinces; (5) Inherit the spirit of the martyrs of the Zhaoh He uprising and resist Japan; (6) Assist the central government in eliminating the Red bandits; (7) Strive for economic construction and strengthen national power; (8) Unite sincerely and support the central government.

Seamen's Party Headquarters

The Chinese Seamen's Special Party Headquarters held a memorial meeting for the Zhaoh He warship incident at 9 AM yesterday morning in the auditorium of the Party Headquarters. More than a hundred committee members, staff, and representatives of various seamen's groups from the Shanghai District Party Headquarters and District Branch attended. After the formal ceremonies, Committee Member Ma Bolin reported on the beginning and end of the Zhaoh He incident, stating that in the autumn of the fourth year of the Republic of China, Yuan Shikai secretly plotted to restore the imperial system. His henchmen were all over the country. Zheng Rucheng, the Shanghai and Songhu garrison commander, was one of them. Mr. Chen Ying Shi, under the order of the Premier, and Comrade Chiang Kai-shek presided over the revolutionary affairs in Shanghai. On December 5, he ordered Mr. Yang Xiaotian to lead more than 20 marines to occupy the Zhaoh He warship. The officers and soldiers of the ship were strictly forbidden to chop the ammunition depot in the cabin with axes, take out ammunition, and fire cannons to attack the manufacturing bureau, firing more than 60 shots. There was no response on land. As they were wondering, the Yingrui and Tongji rebel ships had been heavily bribed by Yuan's army and counterattacked the Zhaoh He, firing several shots that hit the ship, injuring many soldiers of the Zhaoh He. At the same time, Yuan's army was densely deployed on land, cutting off communication. Bolin and more than 20 comrades calmly fought with Mr. Yang Xiaotian. Late at night, there was no support on land, and the rebel ships continued to attack. At the same time, the Zhaoh He's anchor hoisting machine was destroyed by rebel artillery fire and could not be used to hoist the anchor and sail the ship. They had no choice but to temporarily go ashore. Bolin and Mr. Yang Xiaotian braved all kinds of hardships and returned to the general headquarters in the French Concession the next day to pay their respects to Mr. Chen Ying Shi and ask for instructions for another uprising. During the second uprising, Bolin was ordered to go to Humen, where he was intercepted by Li Fulin and sent to Long Jiguang in Guangzhou, where he was detained for more than 50 days. Just in time for the Yunnan uprising, he regained his freedom. At that time, Mr. Yang Xiaotian was the commander of the navy, and Bolin was the commander-in-chief of the marines. This uprising took a lot of effort. Although it was unsuccessful, it chilled Yuan's thieves. Therefore, Yuan died of depression during the Yunnan uprising. This is a great commemoration of our party's overthrow of the old warlords. The meeting adjourned at 11 AM.

Seamen's Union

Yesterday was the 18th anniversary of the Zhaoh He warship uprising. The preparatory committee of the Chinese Seamen's Union held a ceremony at 10 AM in commemoration. More than a hundred people attended, including all the staff and representatives of various seamen's groups in Shanghai. It was originally scheduled for Yang Hu, a standing committee member of the union, to personally report on the incident at the time and his current feelings. However, due to a temporary matter, Secretary Hou Dachun represented the chairman and reported on the incident. Then Secretary Sun Liping and various representatives spoke one after another, and the atmosphere was very enthusiastic, reaching a temporary climax.

Zhaoh He School

The Zhaoh He Middle School, established in memory of the Zhaoh He uprising, held a memorial meeting in the school's auditorium at 8 AM yesterday morning. More than 300 people attended, including all teachers, students, parents, and guests. The inside and outside of the venue were covered with slogans, and a half-mast was flown, creating a very solemn atmosphere. First, Principal Jia, the chairman, reported on the details of the Zhaoh He warship uprising, followed by a speech by Mr. Zheng Xiping, who was familiar with the Zhaoh He uprising. His words were very alert and contained encouragement. The meeting then adjourned.

Ministry of Communications Orders All Shipping Companies to Prohibit Shanghai-Fujian Navigation - Foreign Ships Entering and Leaving Are Also Subject to Inspection

Since the Fujian Incident occurred, the Ministry of Communications, in order to prevent treacherous people from secretly transporting military supplies to support the Fujian side, specially ordered the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau to instruct all commercial shipping companies to temporarily suspend all Shanghai-Fujian routes. If it is necessary to pass through Fuzhou, it is also not allowed to stop. After receiving the order, the bureau immediately instructed the shipping companies to be informed. In addition to the state-run China Merchants Bureau, which had already suspended operations before receiving the order, the Shanghai-Fujian routes of other companies such as Sanbei and Chang'an were immediately suspended after receiving the order and changed routes. As for foreign ships such as Jardine Matheson & Co., they still operate as usual, but they must be inspected by the navy when passing through the mouth of the sea.

News of the Current Situation After the Fujian Incident Comes from the Shipping Industry - Fujian Seaport is Virtually Blockaded - The Market is as Stable as Ever

Since the Fujian Incident occurred, Shanghai has been rumored that the situation on the border between Zhejiang and Fujian is tense. Yesterday, this port received a telegram from Fujian, stating that the situation in Fuzhou has gradually eased. However, foreign ships entering and leaving have been inspected. The true situation in Fujian is described as follows:

Navy Inspects Foreign Ships

When the Fuzhou mutiny started, the central government immediately dispatched the First Fleet of the Navy to Sanduo Bay, ready to blockade the Fujian sea and cut off Fujian's supplies. However, because foreign merchant ships were operating as usual, the naval authorities had no way to block the Fujian port. The situation is now tense, and since the 2nd of this month, it can no longer wait. Therefore, the warships in Sanduo Bay have been dispatched to the port of Fuzhou to inspect all merchant ships coming to and from the port of Fujian. However, domestic ships have already suspended operations. At present, only British and Japanese foreign ships are coming and going. A few days ago, the Hengsheng wheel of Jardine Matheson Company arrived in Fujian from the port. When it entered the port of Fujian, the Yixian warship ordered it to dock and sent officers and soldiers to board the ship to interrogate the passengers in detail, inspect their luggage, and open the cargo hold for inspection. When the ship left Fuzhou, it was the same. Therefore, the sea transportation in Fuzhou is no less than a virtual blockade.

Foreign Merchants Request Exemption from Inspection

The owner of the Hengsheng wheel reported to the Shanghai office of this trip back to Shanghai. The Shanghai office stated that the regular Fuzhou ship Jiesheng must also operate. The Navy's inspection is not necessary. It is heard that the British resident Chinese consul has presented a request to our government for exemption from inspection in order to avoid causing disputes.

Xiamen Ships Operate as Usual

Xiamen is also an important seaport in Fujian Province. Since President Chiang ordered domestic ships not to stop at the coastal ports of Fujian Province, Chinese merchant ships have suspended operations. Foreign ships in the port are still operating as usual. Yesterday, the Dutch ship Zhibada came to Shanghai from Xiamen. According to people on the ship, the authorities in Xiamen, considering that there are many foreigners in Xiamen, especially Taiwanese people, are deeply afraid of causing disputes. Therefore, they still do not inspect foreign ships entering and leaving as usual. However, the transportation of goods in the area has been affected by the situation and has sharply reduced.

Fuzhou Market is Stable

The director of the Fuzhou branch of a British shipping company in Shanghai sent a telegram to Shanghai yesterday, reporting on the recent situation in Fujian Province, stating that the situation in Fujian has gradually eased in recent days, the market is stable, and panic has been slightly reduced. Goods are still being shipped out. Also, according to passengers who arrived in Shanghai on the Hengsheng wheel, the city of Fuzhou has been as usual for the past few days, and even armed soldiers are rarely seen. At the moment, the authorities in Fujian Province are eager to move the government to Zhangzhou. As for the 19th Route Army, most of them have been transferred to the border of Jianou.

The Three Unified Taxes on Cigarettes, Cement, and Matches Were Increased Yesterday - The Unified Tax Office Announced New Tax Rates

The new customs tariff revised by the Ministry of Finance is scheduled to be implemented from January 1 next year. The three unified taxes on cigarettes, cement, and matches were increased yesterday. The new tax rates for cigarettes, etc., announced by the Unified Tax Office yesterday are recorded below: (Matches) Match tax rates were not classified for collection. Now, they are divided into two categories: sulfide and safety. Sulfide matches are divided into two tax rates: A and B. Type A is taxed at 10.8 yuan per large box, and Type B is 13.5 yuan. Safety matches are divided into three tax rates: A, B, and C. Type A is taxed at 13.5 yuan per box, Type B is 17.4 yuan, and Type C is 21 yuan. Small boxes are calculated at one-tenth of the price. (Cigarette Tax Rates: Type A has increased from 55 yuan per 50,000 cigarettes to 80 yuan, and Type B has increased from 95 yuan to 160 yuan.) (Cement) The new cement tax rate is 1.2 yuan for every 170 kilograms, 8 jiao for 113.33 kilograms, 6 jiao for 85 kilograms, 4.6 jiao for 63.5 kilograms, 4 jiao for 56.67 kilograms, 3.6 jiao for 49.9 kilograms, and 2 jiao for 42.2 kilograms.

Manufacturers Firmly Oppose the Increased Cigarette Tax - The Trade Association Will Hold a Meeting Today to Discuss

Dagon Society says that the Ministry of Finance has recently increased the three unified taxes on matches, cement, and cigarettes, starting yesterday, in order to slightly compensate for the fact that the national treasury is in deficit and the military and political expenses are in great need of funds. However, manufacturers have opposed this one after another. The details are recorded below:

Cigarette Trade Will Hold a Meeting Today

The Shanghai Cigarette Trade Association believes that the cigarette business in Shanghai has been declining recently due to weak social purchasing power. Many cigarette factories have closed down. Now, the Ministry of Finance has suddenly increased the unified tax, which will have a major impact on business. Therefore, it is specially scheduled to convene a general meeting at the meeting place on Mei Baige Road at 2 PM today to discuss countermeasures and unanimously request a postponement of the tax. Wang Wenjing, a member of the Cigarette Trade Association, also said that the matter of increasing the cigarette unified tax has been sent to the authorities for consultation on several matters, requesting that the business difficulties be taken into account and the implementation be temporarily postponed. The tax authorities have agreed to forward the request to the Ministry of Finance for instructions, but starting yesterday, all products from various factories have been taxed according to the new regulations.

The Tax Office States That It Is Handling Matters Under Orders

According to the person in charge of the Tax Office, the Tax Office is handling this increase in the unified tax under the order of the Ministry. If manufacturers have any opinions, the Tax Office can only forward the original intentions to the higher level. All measures must be decided by the Ministry of Finance. The Tax Office has no authority to approve them alone. In the future, cigarettes from various factories will not be allowed to leave the factory without new stamps. Otherwise, they will be detained.

The Increase in Comparison of New and Old Tax Rates

The cigarette unified tax has always used 50,000 cigarettes as the standard. The old tax rates are divided into two levels: the first level is taxed at 95 yuan for those with a selling price of more than 260 yuan, and the second level is taxed at 55 yuan for those with a selling price of less than 260 yuan. The new tax rate is that the first level is for those with a selling price of more than 300 yuan and taxed at 160 yuan (65 yuan more than before), and the second level is for those with a selling price of less than 300 yuan and taxed at 80 yuan (25 yuan more than before). However, the above is calculated for 50,000 cigarettes. If calculated for each can (50 cigarettes), only 6.5 fen and 2.5 fen are added. For each pack (10 cigarettes), only 12 copper coins are added. Therefore, according to the Tax Office, the amount is not very large.

Municipal Government Prepares for Relocation: 15th Committee Meeting; Relocation of Various Bureaus and Offices Already Determined

The Shanghai Municipal Government Relocation Preparatory Committee held its 15th meeting at the Municipal Government at 3 PM on the 4th. The committee members present were Shen Gao, Tan Wenqing, Dong Tianyou (representing Tan Wenqing), Jing Song, Lin Wenquan (representing Cui Jinhua), Chen Jun (representing Lu Binpu), He Xiang, Zhang Binghui (representing Sun Xiaoyi), Li Dachao, Mi Jifang, and Zhou Zhaonan (representing Zhou Zhaonan). The meeting was chaired by Li Dachao and proceeded as scheduled. (A) Report Matters: The chairman reported on issues such as the central district market, schools, and transportation, and submitted them to the mayor, who assigned them to the Public Works Bureau, Health Bureau, Education Bureau, Public Utilities Bureau, and the Xingye Trust Company for preparation. Committee member Shen Gao reported (omitted). Various committee members reported the scheduled relocation times for various bureaus and offices: Health Bureau on the 25th, Education Bureau on the 26th, Public Works Bureau on the 26th, Land Bureau not yet determined, Social Affairs Bureau on the 20th, and Secretariat on the 25th. (B) Discussion Matters: (1) Regarding the case of keeping the keys to the temporary houses of various bureaus, it was resolved that after the bureaus take over, the keys will be temporarily kept by the resident personnel of the new Municipal Government building. (2) Regarding the relocation expenses of various bureaus and offices, it was resolved that the various bureaus and offices should directly submit them to the Municipal Government for approval. (3) Regarding the installation of telephones and electric lights in various offices, it was resolved that for the telephones required by various bureaus, the bureaus should directly notify the Public Utilities Bureau to handle them; for the electric lights, the bureaus should install them themselves. (4) Regarding the establishment of a public cafeteria, it was resolved that the opinions of relevant bureaus should be solicited to decide whether to jointly or separately handle it, and to investigate the past catering expenses and opinions of various bureaus in order to solicit merchants to undertake it. (5) Regarding the fees for water meters, electric meters, and hot water heaters in the temporary houses of various bureaus, it was resolved to petition the Municipal Government to establish a Central District Management Office to manage the repair of public buildings and the expenses for water, electricity, and hot water heaters. (6) Regarding the method of delivering official documents after the relocation of the Municipal Government, it was resolved to appoint committee members Shen Gao, Tan Wenqing, and Zhang Binghui to draft a method. (7) Regarding the parking spaces and the construction of gas stations for various bureaus and offices, it was resolved to send a letter to the Central District Construction Committee to designate locations for handling. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Shanghai-Guangdong Flights Departed as Usual Yesterday; Normal Landings at Fuzhou Station; Damaged Aircraft No. 16 Transported to Shanghai

Japanese Expel Overseas Chinese; Overseas Chinese Being Expelled

Chinese laborers and restaurant owners Zhang Maoqing, Zheng Jiaxiang, Pan Ding-san, Pan Hong-ba, Chen Shun-huai, Chen Bao-hui, Guo Yu-guang, Jiang De-fang, Wang Ming-cai, Zhang Ming-ji, Xia Rui-chang, Wang Yu-biao, and others, totaling more than twenty people, in Japanese ports such as Yokohama, Nagoya, and Kobe, were unable to find work in Japan. The Japanese authorities, on the pretext that these unemployed overseas Chinese should return to their home country, put them on Japanese ships and forbade them from going to Japan again. These overseas Chinese were mostly from Qingtian, Ruian, and Fuzhou areas of Zhejiang. They were expelled back to Shanghai yesterday, their travel expenses exhausted, and their situation was dire. Most of them went to Nanshi and temporarily stayed in small inns before returning to their hometowns.

Voyages to Japan Nearly Extinct

Since the Japanese shipping companies announced new regulations for overseas Chinese traveling to Japan, effective December 1st, requiring a deposit of 100 yen and deducting various expenses, such as the cost of returning to China if landing is denied, from this deposit, the number of Chinese businessmen and laborers traveling to Japan has almost completely stopped. Most laborers and small businessmen do not have the financial capacity and cannot bear the various mistreatments. Therefore, the passenger business of Japanese ships in Shanghai has plummeted. The number of third-class passengers on each outbound ship is only one-tenth of what it was last month.

Japanese Merchants' Shipping Industry in Decline; Even with Government Subsidies, It is Still Useless; Forced to Operate, Chinese Compradors Are Constantly Complaining

The New Voice News Agency reports that the Japanese shipping company Nisshin Kisen Kaisha mainly operates routes along the Yangtze River, followed by routes in the North and South Seas, all of which are Chinese routes. Since the September 18th and January 28th Incidents, the company has been affected by the Chinese boycott, and 24 ships have been successively suspended. In order to maintain the original routes, the Japanese government provided subsidies, and the company resumed the Yangtze River routes with four ships, the Luoyang Maru, Xiangyang Maru, Nanyang Maru, and Fengyang Maru, and the North and South Seas routes with four ships, the Huashan Maru, Songshan Maru, Lushan Maru, and Tangshan Maru, for a total of eight ships. Despite repeated price reductions to attract customers, the company's efforts to recover have been ineffective. It was forced to either sell or dismantle nine ships, including the Daifuku and Dairi, that had been suspended, and there is still no possibility of recovery. Each time goods are imported and exported, except for Japanese transit goods, Chinese goods are absent. The income from passenger fares and freight charges is not enough to cover the operating expenses of the ships. Although the company receives subsidies from the Japanese government, the Chinese compradors are constantly complaining. If there is no turnaround, it will be useless, and the ships that are forced to operate will inevitably be completely suspended, resulting in liquidation.

Shanghai County Levies the Second Term of Land Value Tax: Autumn Inspection Reduces Actual Levy; Deadline is the End of February Next Year

Shanghai County's land value tax for the second term of the 22nd year was officially opened by the county government on the 1st of this month, with a deadline of three months, until the end of February of the 23rd year. Late payments will be subject to late payment penalties. Yesterday, the county government announced the amount payable per mu for this term to all businesses in the county for their information. It is calculated that the superior land of the 16th, 18th, and 21st Baos, together with the surcharges, is 5 jiao 9 fen 7 li per mu, with the actual levy after the autumn inspection being 5 jiao 4 fen 9 li 2 hao. The standard land is 6 jiao 2 fen 3 li 5 hao per mu, with the actual levy after the autumn inspection being 5 jiao 7 fen 3 li 6 hao. The superior standard land of the 24th and 26th Baos is 6 jiao 2 fen 3 li 5 hao per mu, including surcharges, with the actual levy after the autumn inspection being 5 jiao 7 fen 3 li 6 hao.

Questioning the Police

Regarding the arrest, Lawyer Xu Jie said at the law firm that at 5 PM yesterday, this lawyer, accompanied by Mr. Li Shi-chang, representative of the Kim Seok family, went to the Lou-za-wan French Police Station to visit Political Director Harri and questioned him on the spot as follows: (Question) (Lawyer Xu): Is there a fact that Kim Seok, a citizen of the Republic of China, was arrested by your police station? (Answer): We were only assisting at the request of the Japanese consul. (Question): Is Kim Seok still being held at your police station? (Answer): He was already taken away by the Japanese consulate. (Question): How long was he detained at your police station, and on what day was he handed over to the Japanese consulate? (Answer): He was not detained at the police station. His family has presented it to your police station. (Answer): Kim Seok did not have his citizenship permit with him. If he had presented his naturalization permit at the time, he would not have been taken away by the Japanese police. (Question): Kim Seok claims to be Korean. Does your police station have a record of his confession? (Answer): There is no record of his confession. (Question): Why didn't the police station investigate Kim Seok's nationality? (Answer): Because he admitted it himself, there was no need to investigate. (Question): If you do not investigate based on the suspect's confession, your police station will be deceived. (Answer): The suspect admitted it himself, so the police station did not need to investigate. (Question): This year, Kim Cheol and Kim Seok, father and son, were arrested in the same way. After submitting their citizenship certificates, they were released. Your police station should know that Kim Seok is a Chinese citizen based on your duties. (Answer): I don't know about this year's arrest. (Question): According to Article 7 of the Agreed Rules for the Establishment of Chinese Courts in the French Concession, the arrested suspect should first be questioned by the competent court and not be transferred to government offices outside the concession. Kim Seok is a citizen of the Republic of China and should be transferred to the Chinese court. (Answer): I really didn't know that Kim Seok had been naturalized as a Chinese citizen and obtained Chinese citizenship, and he himself admitted that he was Korean. (Question): Now that it has been proven that Kim Seok is a citizen, your police station should take Kim Seok back from the Japanese consulate. If he is suspected of a crime, he should be handed over to the Chinese court; otherwise, he should be released. (Answer): This is a matter of negotiation between China and Japan. The French police station cannot help. (Question): Kim Seok was handed over to the Japanese consulate by your police station. Your police station should take him back. (Answer): This matter requires requesting the French consul to consult with the Japanese consulate. Because it was late, we said goodbye to Mr. Li and left.

Should Delivery Notes Be Affixed with Stamps? The Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Food Industry Association Sends a Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for Explanation

The Shanghai Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Food Food Industry Association has recently received reports from various member factories, companies, and stores that the Shangbao Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau has ordered the shops to affix stamps to the delivery notes they issue, and has imposed severe penalties for non-compliance. Furthermore, the Bureau even found that the Dehua Biscuit Factory on Zhaozhou Road had affixed a stamp worth one cent to a receipt with a value of 88 cents, and accused them of not affixing a sufficient number of stamps, which was inappropriate. Yesterday, the Association sent a letter to the Shangbao County Committee for the Trial of Violations of the Stamp Tax Regulations, asking them to withdraw the original case and re-examine it. They also sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for explanation. The letter stated: "Our Association has found that shops are required to issue delivery notes to customers every month for all outstanding payments for verification, and then go to collect the payments when they are due. These delivery notes only contain the nature of requesting payment and verifying whether there are any errors in the quantity. Before the customer seeks payment, they must be listed in detail and sent every month. If the customer delays payment, the delivery note must also be issued monthly and cannot be omitted. Therefore, these delivery notes do not involve the transfer of money, so most of them do not affix stamps. When the payment is received and a receipt is issued, the stamps are affixed in accordance with the regulations. This is an exercise of obligation under the principle of parallel rights and obligations, and there is no doubt about it. However, the Stamp Tax Bureau does not have clear regulations on whether this type of delivery note should be affixed with stamps, and relies on its one-sided whims to impose heavy fines on the grounds of not affixing stamps. Our Association has repeatedly received reports from its members, who all say that if they affix stamps to each delivery note, they cannot afford it; if they do not affix stamps, they are at risk of being heavily fined. They are in a dilemma and at a loss. We are sending a special letter to your Association to ask for an explanation, so that we can follow it and alleviate the merchants' difficulties." Suddenly Abducted, Rich Merchant Yang Shousheng From Suzhou

The case of Yang Shousheng, a rich merchant from Suzhou residing in front of the old county government office in Nanshi, who was kidnapped by bandits near the back door of his residence on Guangqi Road at 6 PM on the 6th of last month, has been reported in detail in this newspaper. However, since the case occurred, Public Security Bureau Chief Wen Hong-en has been unusually attentive and has repeatedly ordered his subordinates to solve the case within a limited time. Unfortunately, the bandits are cunning and try their best to avoid the eyes of the arresting officers. Yang escaped safely some days ago. According to news from Yang's residence, Yang has indeed escaped danger and is currently recuperating in the hospital and has not returned home. It is said that Yang was in the bandits' den for a total of 26 days. The bandits were heavily guarded, making it difficult to escape. One day, Yang pretended to be asleep and overheard the guards whispering to each other that the rumors outside were very tight, the detectives were investigating, and it was probably necessary to move to another location. On this day, it became clear that Yang was about to be moved. Two guards helped him out of the plain house. He saw that the place resembled a township and instantly arrived in the fields. One of the guards, who had been with Yang for a long time and was more amiable than the other bandits, was persuaded by Yang to abandon evil and return to righteousness. The guard expressed his sympathy, but lamented that there was no opportunity to help him escape. At this time, Yang had an idea and said to him, "I need to relieve myself." The guard helped him to the field, while the other acted as a lookout because the sky was already breaking and people were gradually becoming visible. Yang said to the guard who was helping him, "Help me, now is the time!" The guard went to the lookout to pretend to look for toilet paper. Yang took the opportunity to stand up and ran wildly away from the guard. After about a quarter of an hour, he saw electric lights and a road, seemingly near the Sun Temple. He immediately took a rickshaw to his relative's house. At that time, he was like a drunken man. His relative sent him to the hospital for recuperation. The doctor said that Yang's nerves were very weak and that he needed to go to a quiet place for recuperation. It is likely that his family will accompany him to Hangzhou for recuperation.

The Reason for the Suicide of Guo Shaoheng, Chief Officer of the Jiang’an Ship: Economic Pressure Due to Multiple Wives

The suicide of Guo Shaoheng, Chief Officer of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company’s Jiang’an ship, has been reported in this newspaper. The reason for his suicide was unclear. After repeated investigations by reporters, it was learned that it was due to having multiple wives and economic pressure, which led him to become disillusioned with life. The details of what was learned are recorded as follows:

Fond of Women

Guo Shaoheng served as the leading officer on the Jiang’an ship since it was built, serving in this role for more than ten years. He usually had no faults and was highly valued by the ship owners. However, he was fond of women throughout his life. Whenever the ship arrived in Shanghai or Hankou and was docked with nothing to do, he would often go out alone to seek pleasure, regardless of appearance, and would accept them all. Therefore, in addition to his legal wife, he had three concubines residing in Hong Kong, Shanghai, and Hankou. How could he maintain several households with a meager salary of one hundred and eighty yuan? As a result, he experienced economic panic, which ultimately led to his suicide.

Difficult to Meet his Wives

In addition to his family on Haining Road in Shanghai, Guo also had a family in Hankou, with numerous children. Furthermore, he frequently engaged in extramarital affairs, leading to increased economic pressure. Consequently, household expenses were often depleted. It is said that his wife from Hong Kong came to Shanghai this time to demand money from Guo and discuss future living arrangements. Unable to cope with this situation, Guo Shaoheng committed suicide. After his death, a search of his bedroom revealed that he did not have a single penny, which further highlighted his economic distress.

Haunted House

After Guo's suicide, he left a letter in his room addressed to Huang Fengqi, asking him to cancel the lease for the new house he had rented in Zhabei. According to the letter, he decided to cancel the lease because ghostly apparitions had been discovered in the new house, making it impossible to live there in peace. As a result, some people speculated that since Guo had thoughts of suicide and his spirit was weakened, he was being haunted by ghosts.

Many Photos

Many photos of women were found in his bedroom, as well as several nude model photos. Guo also had handwritten words, the gist of which was that all the blood and energy of his life had been sacrificed for this. Currently, his body has been collected by his family in Shanghai and will be sent to the Guangzhao Villa for storage. The Jiang’an ship has already left Shanghai.

Prostitute Keeper Wang Caiying Sentenced to Imprisonment for Forcing a Woman into Prostitution

Zhu Hongbao, a young woman in her early twenties, with a beautiful appearance, was a native of Wuzhen, Zhejiang. Two years ago, she married Lu A’da, who worked as a boatman. Lu lived on his boat, so he was unable to stay with his beautiful wife. As a result, Zhu became acquainted with Lu A’bao. In the summer of this year, A’bao lured Zhu to Shanghai with sweet words and sold her to Wang Pengying, a woman who ran a brothel at No. 507 Zhejiang Road. Thus, Zhu fell into the fire pit. Regardless of wind, rain, or snow, she had to stand on the street every night to solicit customers. Sometimes, she had to entertain two or three customers per night. If she had no customers for a day, she would be subjected to severe beatings. This kind of life was no different from hell, but the brothel keeper only knew how to make a lot of money and did not care about the happiness and suffering of the prostitutes. She was afraid that the prostitutes would escape, so she ordered the maid to closely monitor them when they went out to solicit customers and did not allow them to step beyond the boundaries. Even if they were sick, they were not allowed to see a doctor and were forced to entertain customers. Many women had lost their lives in this place. Zhu has only been engaged in this lowly profession for a few months, but she has experienced all the bitterness of it. She wanted to escape from the fire pit, but she had no chance. On the 27th of last month, she found an opportunity to report to Wang Hailin and other Chinese detectives of the Lao Zha police, who arrested Wang and the maid, Li. Wu Zhangshi was also arrested and handed over to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Feng Shide sentenced Wang Caiying to two years and six months in prison, Li to two months in prison, and Wu Zhangshi was acquitted.

The Preparatory Committee of the Civilian Factory Held a Meeting Yesterday Morning to Discuss Progress; The Cost of House Repairs Was Extremely High; Half of the Funds Were Reduced and Work Is Proceeding Actively

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has established a Civilian Factory at the Civilian Residence in Gaojing Temple to provide relief to unemployed workers in the war zone. The plan had already been approved by the Municipal Government, and a preparatory committee was formed to oversee everything. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, the preparatory committee members held another meeting at the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to discuss reducing repair costs and various progress plans. The details are recorded as follows:

Motivation for Establishing the Factory

Since the January 28th Incident, the homes in Wusong and Zhabei were destroyed, and countless victims of the disaster were displaced and homeless. In view of this, the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee allocated 30,000 yuan to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to provide relief. Wu Xingya, the director of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, proposed establishing a Civilian Factory to accommodate unemployed workers in the war zone. A plan was drafted, a preparatory committee was organized, and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and reported to the Ministry of Industry for record.

First to Establish Carpentry and Other Departments

The establishment of the Civilian Factory is purely for the purpose of providing relief to unemployed workers in the war zone. However, due to limited funds, it will be implemented in stages. If successful, it will be expanded. The first phase will establish carpentry, copperware, straw weaving, printing, and leather goods departments, with a provisional quota of 40 workers. Because the equipment for the above five departments is relatively simple, they will be opened first.

Affiliated Training Institute

After the establishment of the Civilian Factory, a training institute will be affiliated to the carpentry department. If necessary, other departments will be added. Unemployed workers in the city who pass the examination of the institute can be admitted, but only food and lodging will be provided, without additional salary. Most of the staff will be concurrently managed by the staff of the Social Affairs Bureau to save expenses. Other full-time staff who must be hired will also be those who are willing to fulfill their obligations as a principle.

Reduced Repair Costs

The preparatory committee of the Civilian Factory believes that providing relief to unemployed workers in the war zone cannot be delayed. Therefore, a meeting was convened this morning to discuss reducing renovation costs and various progress plans. Zhang Zhenyuan, Chen Lengseng, Wang Gang, Chen Baohua, Qin Hongji, and other five members attended the meeting. As a result of the discussion, because the Civilian Residence buildings in Gaojing Temple were poorly constructed, many were blown down during the previous storm. Therefore, major repairs were needed. The Municipal Public Works Bureau estimated that the renovation would cost more than 6,000 yuan. However, due to limited funds, it was decided to reduce it to 3,000 yuan, and repair one-third of the Civilian Residence buildings first. The rest will be expanded after raising additional funds. However, the area is all muddy land, and it is difficult to walk after heavy rain. It is also necessary to find ways to add coal ash. Therefore, it is too late to start construction this year, and it must be postponed to February or March of next spring before it can be opened.

Hu Xialian's Embezzlement Case Scheduled for Sentencing

Tong He, a Shandong woman, 41 years old, currently resides at No. 17 Shijian Tou, Huazhan Wharf, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Pudong. Her husband, Tong Guogui, worked as a tea servant on the Xinkang ship of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company’s Northern Shipping Line. Hu Xialian, a Shandong native who worked as a detective in Renchang Li, K’ai-tse-erh Road, French Concession, was Tong's sworn brother. After Tong's death, Hu accompanied Tong's wife, He, to China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to negotiate. As a result, she received a pension of 500 yuan, which Hu also accompanied her to collect. Later, Hu kept the money in custody. The following year, in February, He, believing that her husband had died and she could not stay in Shanghai for long, planned to withdraw the money from Hu to return to her hometown. Hu told her that he had lent 200 yuan to his friend Wang Desheng, and he did not have the other 300 yuan on him. Moreover, as a woman, it would be inconvenient for her to carry a large sum of cash home. You are illiterate and don't know what's good for you, so you should go back first, and I will send the money to you on your behalf. Tong He trusted Hu as her husband's sworn brother and did not suspect any changes, believing him to be telling the truth. Therefore, she only withdrew a small amount of travel expenses and took her children back to her hometown, counting on Hu to send the money home so that she could rely on it to live on. Unexpectedly, after arriving home, she waited a long time but did not see Hu send the money. So she sent a letter to Hu to inquire, but Hu ignored her and did not reply. In May of this year, she had no choice but to bring her children to Shanghai to ask Hu for the money. Hu initially hesitated, but then denied keeping it on her behalf, trying to embezzle it, causing a dispute and quarrel. After mediation failed, He hired lawyer Yang Zhihao to file a criminal self-lawsuit with the Second Special Court, accusing Hu of embezzlement and attaching a civil lawsuit to recover 429 yuan in pension. The Water Outage Dispute in Bolu and Other Neighborhoods is Becoming More Serious; The Lives of More Than 2,000 Residents are in Danger

Due to the increase in water costs after the British-owned Shanghai Waterworks Company implemented a water meter system for charging fees, the water costs have exceeded more than 30% of the rent. The owners of the buildings in Bolu Li, Bofu Li, Boshou Li, three male houses, and more than two hundred houses between Pingliang Road and Yangzhou Road in eastern Shanghai, are unable to bear this additional loss and have delayed payment. The water company removed the water meters in the three neighborhoods and cut off the water supply because they did not pay the water bill. The tenants of the neighborhood have repeatedly protested, opening up the fire hydrants in the neighborhood to maintain the water supply temporarily. Recently, the water company used coercive measures to close the fire hydrants, claiming that no water bills have been paid to date and that the fire hydrants have been open for several months, resulting in uncompensated losses. The tenants of the neighborhood panicked and jointly petitioned the owners, demanding that they pay the water bills and open the water supply to maintain their lives. They also opened the fire hydrants on the road themselves. At the same time, the owners reported to the Real Estate Association, requesting them to negotiate with the Municipal Council. Yesterday, the water company sent workers to close the fire hydrants on the road. The tenants became more panicked and negotiated with the owners again. The owners and the Real Estate Association petitioned the Municipal Council, requesting that the water company be instructed to open the water supply. Board Member He Dequi met them and listened to the opinions of the representatives, including Kui Yanfang. Board Member He then conveyed the information to General Manager Zhong Si, who said that if the water supply was to be opened, the owner must pay the water bill in full. Although Board Member Bao mediated and asked the owner to pay a certain amount first, with the remainder to be paid in installments, the General Manager insisted on not agreeing, resulting in a deadlock. The matter concerns the lives of more than a thousand people in the three neighborhoods and it is said that it has aroused serious resistance. They are requesting assistance from all walks of life to achieve the goal of opening the water supply.

The Young Kidnapped Boy, Qie Bao, Died in the Bandit's Den; Zhang Shuchuan, the Main Culprit in This Case, Confessed in Court Yesterday

Sun Yushun, a native of Shaoxing who lives at No. 115 Han’an Li, Ximen Road, French Concession, had his five-year-old only son, Qie Bao, suddenly disappear while playing in front of the door at noon on May 20th of this year. On August 14th, Zheng's wife, Zhou, concubine, Lou, Zheng's friend, Qiu Yaoshan, Zheng's apprentices, Li Ziqing and Min Xinting, and Min's lover, Zhou Wenying, were arrested in Room 516 of the Far East Hotel on Tibet Road. On the morning of the 27th of last month, Inspector Jin Jiulin, the Director of the Special Agency of the French Police, and detectives arrested Zhang Shuchuan, also known as Da Kaizi, from Jiangbei Yancheng, from Run’an Li. He was handed over to the Second Special District Court for detention and investigation, and the case was combined with the previous arrests for trial. All the details were reported in this newspaper on the 29th of last month. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Li Changnian interrogated the case in the First Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, explained the police's investigation process. Then, Zhang confessed that he had initiated the kidnapping alone and hid the child at Yu Dashunzi’s home at No. 121 Zhujiawan, Zhongshan Road, Zhabei. I wrote three letters to the plaintiff, and sent one to a letterbox. The first one told the owner not to worry, the child was safe. The second one demanded 8,000 yuan. The third one cut a piece of cloth from the child's clothes and sent it to the plaintiff as proof. The other four letters were not written by me. I only wrote the envelopes. The letters were written by Dong Zhiqing and his friend Zhang. I put these four letters in the postbox at Caojiadu. The child became ill after more than ten days. I gave him several doses of Huichun Dan, but it didn't work. He died on May 18th. I put the body in a wooden box, covered it with a hemp bag, and carried it to the Xiaobin River in Lujiazhai, Zhongshan Road. I was scared and didn't want the money, but Yu, Dong, and Zhang insisted on writing letters and demanding money. I didn't know anything about the money. At this point, the court gave Zhang paper and pen, ordered him to sit in the press seats, and copy the phrases in the letters for handwriting verification. After Zhang finished writing, the court ordered the six people who had been arrested earlier, including Qiu Yaoshan, to the dock and asked if they knew Zhang. They all replied that they did not know him. Then, the victim Sun Yushun stated that Zhang's father was in charge of Run’an Li, and Zhang had been sweeping the streets for several years. How could they not know each other? And before Qiu and the others were arrested, they had been seen talking at the entrance of the lane. Zhang cannot do this alone, and there must be accomplices who have not been arrested. He requested a thorough investigation and search for the child’s body. By this point, it was past noon. The court, believing that the facts of the case were unclear, and that there were many doubts, ordered a thorough investigation before scheduling another hearing. The defendants were returned to custody separately, and nearly twenty letters from the victim were handed over to the investigating detective for further investigation. During the trial, the child’s mother, Sun He, listened to Zhang's confession about her child's death from the sidelines, feeling heartache and shedding tears. As she left the court, she was helped by her relatives. Onlookers were saddened and heartbroken, and cursed the kidnappers as unscrupulous.

The exorbitant fees charged by the telephone company in Pudong prompt opposition from telephone users, who demand uniformity with the urban area and the elimination of water line fees

The Guomin News Agency reports that after the Pudong Telephone Bureau announced its rates (12 yuan for residential, 15 yuan for commercial, 5 yuan more than Nanshi due to water lines), Pudong users collectively protested, arguing that the water lines were the Bureau's business tool (commonly known as "making money"). There is no precedent in the world for charging customers for the cost of generating income, and it is also unfair to single out Pudong users to bear this monthly water line maintenance fee of 5 yuan. Furthermore, communication with the Chinese concession is restricted, with an additional charge of 5 cents for each call exceeding the limit, while a 5 yuan maintenance fee for communication with the Chinese concession is also collected when applying for installation. All these charges seem almost ingenious. The existence of telephones in Pudong was the result of a proposal made by the representatives of the Five Districts Conference in the spring of the 18th year of the Republic to promote the prosperity of Pudong, requesting the Ministry to establish the Pudong Telephone Bureau. The Bureau has been completed for three years, but it only formally opened at the end of last month due to water line negotiations. Now, the high fees make it unaffordable for the public to apply for installation, which not only directly affects the development of the Bureau's business, but also indirectly hinders the prosperity of the Pudong market. It is reported that the Pudong Chamber of Commerce, the Fifth District Party Headquarters, and others have successively petitioned higher authorities to forward their requests to the Ministry to revise the Pudong telephone rates, to make them uniform with the urban area, to reduce the burden on the public, and to accelerate the prosperity of Pudong.

The Ministry of Railways stipulates that the charging method for chartered cars crossing the river will be calculated in accordance with Articles 32 and 33 of the Passenger Transport Regulations

Regarding the calculation method of the cost of passengers reserving first, second, and third class carriages to cross the river, the Ministry of Railways yesterday specially telegraphed the administrations of the two railways to comply with it. The original text is extracted and recorded as follows:

Telegram from the Ministry of Railways

For the Beijing-Hankou, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Ningbo Railway Bureaus: Regarding the case of the Beining Railway inquiring about the cost of chartered cars transporting Dong Feng across the river, it is found that the so-called chartered car refers to the first, second, and third class passenger cars exclusively reserved by passengers, and the chartered flower cars, chartered cars, or small chartered cars. After separate review and approval, if it is a first, second, or third class passenger car for exclusive use, the river crossing fee for the first part of the car should be charged in accordance with the provisions of Article 32 of the Passenger Transport Regulations promulgated by the Ministry. For example, each first class passenger car must purchase at least 20 first class tickets, and the passenger river crossing fee should also be calculated based on at least 20 first class tickets. The remaining second and third classes should be handled separately in accordance with the provisions of that article. If the chartered car is a flower car, chartered car, or small chartered car, etc., and the number of passengers is sufficient to meet the number stipulated in that article, the original price and passenger river crossing fee should be charged separately with reference to the above method and level, but no additional car rental will be charged. If the number of passengers is less than the number stipulated in Article 32, in addition to the passenger river crossing fee being charged according to the number of passengers, a car rental fee for crossing the river should be charged with reference to the chartered car type and the types stipulated by each road, calculated in 10 kg units. In addition to the separate telegram, you should comply with it immediately. Minister Gu Mengyu (seal)

Passenger Transport Regulations

Attached is the original text of Article 32 of the Passenger Transport Regulations: The minimum number of passenger tickets that should be purchased for reserved vehicles, regardless of the type of vehicle reserved, is a minimum of 35 yuan per car. Each first class passenger car must purchase at least 20 first class tickets, each second class passenger car must purchase at least 35 second class tickets, each third class passenger car must purchase at least 50 third class tickets, and each mixed car must purchase at least half the number of passenger tickets of each class as previously stipulated. Also, the original text of Article 33 of the Passenger Transport Regulations: The rental fees for chartered cars and flower cars are as follows: (1) Flower car: 3 jiao 5 fen per kilometer, with a minimum of 50 yuan; (2) Chartered car: 2 jiao 5 fen per kilometer, with a minimum of 35 yuan; (3) Small chartered car: 1 jiao 5 fen per kilometer, with a minimum of 20 yuan. In addition to the above car rental fees, passengers still pay fares according to the number of people and calculated at the first class rate, and servants pay fares according to the number of people and calculated at the second class rate. All existing equipment in the car is not charged separately, but those attached to special express trains should pay the additional special express train fee according to the number of passenger tickets.

The Shanghai Bar Association is approved to use regular paper for non-litigation matters

The Shanghai Bar Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Judicial Administration regarding whether the regulations of judicial stamp paper rule six applied to documents used in non-litigation events that would require stamp duty: "In investigations concerning non-litigation affairs brought before the courts, it is found that there are no defined legal provisions to rely on regarding the documents used. Consequently, considering the current facts, some use the Department-issued judicial paper, while others affix a judicial stamp paper of one corner, in accordance with rule six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations. The approach has not been uniform from the beginning, and there is often confusion about which to follow. However, if one applies Article One of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations, which states, 'For civil or criminal litigation, unless verbal communication is permitted by law, judicial stamp paper must be used,' it is clear that matters designated as 'non-litigation' do not fall under the scope of litigation. According to the aforementioned article, there is no need to purchase judicial stamp paper. Furthermore, Article Six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations states, 'For submitting documents to judicial organs, those that should use Department-issued paper according to the rules of litigation stamp paper are not required to affix judicial stamp paper; all others must affix judicial stamp paper.' It is apparent from these rules that litigation documents should use Department-issued paper, while other documents submitted to judicial organs should affix a judicial stamp paper of one corner. Given that non-litigation events are not governed by the litigation stamp paper regulations, they naturally fall under the category that requires affixing judicial stamp paper. In summary, it is clear beyond doubt that documents presented to judicial organs in connection with non-litigation events are subject to rule six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations, which requires affixing a one-corner stamp. However, at present, lower-level judicial organs sometimes require people seeking redress for non-litigation matters to purchase Department-issued paper, which has no basis in the codified rules and regulations, and is a result of not fully grasping the application of judicial paper regulations and judicial stamp paper regulations. Moreover, if one must purchase Department-issued paper to file a non-litigation case, then all documents filed with judicial organs must be uniformly required to use Department-issued paper. In that case, rule six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations would be redundant. However, at present, procedures for non-litigation cases differ, and there is no clear consensus. Without a clear explanation from the Ministry, it will be impossible to achieve uniformity. Therefore, we request that the Ministry clarify whether rule six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations applies to documents used in non-litigation cases, requiring affixation of a one-corner stamp, so that we may comply accordingly. We eagerly await instructions.” It is now known that the Ministry of Judicial Administration has issued the following instruction: "Noted. Petitions regarding non-litigation matters do not require the purchase of stamp paper. However, a filing fee must be paid, and stamp paper must be affixed in accordance with Rule Six of the Judicial Stamp Paper Regulations. Notify accordingly." This approval.

Miscellaneous News

Yuan Kuntang Robbed and Loses Father: Yuan Kuntang, a rice merchant from Liuhe working in Beishi, received an urgent letter from his family in his hometown a few days ago. A messenger also reported that his father's old illness had relapsed. Despite recent medical treatment, it had been ineffective. They urged Yuan to return home quickly. Upon hearing this, Yuan borrowed 50 dollars from his colleagues and immediately set off. In the afternoon, he took a long-distance bus to Liuhe. It was already dark when he got off. Realizing he still had five or six li to reach home, Yuan bought a lantern and hurried. About one or two li from his house, three bandits suddenly appeared, blocking his way and threatening him with guns. They robbed him of about 70 silver dollars, taking everything. Yuan shouted for help but was slashed in the arm by the bandits. Deeply distressed after the robbery, Yuan endured the pain and rushed home. To his dismay, upon arrival, his father had already passed away. Having had his money stolen, Yuan rushed to Shanghai yesterday to prepare clothes and other necessities to return and prepare his father's coffin.

Random Thoughts

The Two-Wheeled Class and the Four-Wheeled Class

— Qian Renkang

Shanghai's status as a metropolis stems from many factors, but it could not be so prosperous without bustling roads laid out in a crisscross pattern. The hustle and bustle of the roads is largely due to the embellishment of various vehicles. Among these vehicles, the more prestigious are naturally automobiles and private rickshaws.

Everything has "classes" these days, so let's tentatively call the gentlemen who ride private rickshaws the "two-wheeled class" and the gentlemen who ride automobiles the "four-wheeled class."

Whether it's the "two-wheeled class" or the "four-wheeled class," everyone has a rickshaw puller or chauffeur. The rickshaw puller has to also serve as the driving force for the carriage, naturally suffering much more in life than the chauffeur, and their status is far below that of the chauffeur. Not only below the chauffeur, but below all the drivers. Not only below all the drivers, but some even consider them below the livestock. Because their rickshaws not only carry people, but sometimes the people in the rickshaw also bring a 巴哈 dog. As for the other drivers, their status is naturally much higher. The spirited chauffeur goes without saying, and even the carriage driver who spends all day with animals can still occasionally raise his whip to strike the horse's back a few times, his status certainly not below the livestock.

In this case, the "two-wheeled class" who ride private rickshaws are clearly not very "humane," and the most imposing, most humane, and most "civilized" are naturally the "four-wheeled class" who ride automobiles. Many gentlemen have risen from the "two-wheeled class" to the "four-wheeled class," probably for this reason? Look at the blaring horns, everyone avoids them; like lightning, they speed along freely, truly powerful and influential! However, they sometimes inevitably get cursed as "市虎," probably because they occasionally run over a few people. But the reason people get run over, it is said, is because "one" is not careful. The automobile itself is still very "civilized" and very "humane"!

The Swinification of Life

— Zhou Limin

"Outlook on life" is an abstract term, quite philosophical, with broad and deep meaning. In a narrow sense, it refers to people's way of life, their attitude towards the world, and the concepts they hold. Whether they are optimistic, pessimistic, enlightened, or ×-istic, in short, each person has their own outlook on life, as different as their faces. "Pig," "pighead," "fat pig," "×-pig," these are nicknames for people who are mere clothes hangers and refuse collectors, and also insults for a generation of talentless people.

Isn't this abuse of the word "pig"? If pigs had knowledge, they would surely cry injustice! No, absolutely not; everyone knows that the life of a pig is extremely simple, with no particular pig-life outlook. Here are six ways to encompass it:

First way: Eat... sleep... excrete.

Second way: Sleep... eat... excrete.

Third way: Excrete... sleep... eat.

Fourth way: Eat... excrete... sleep.

Fifth way: Sleep... excrete... eat.

Sixth way: Excrete... eat... sleep.

The life of a pig is nothing more than this. Besides this, there is no concept of diligence, no sense of responsibility to do one's best, exert oneself to the utmost, and die only after one's task is done. Perhaps the pig's so-called pig-life outlook is just like that?

I believe that the unemployed vagrants who rely on their ancestors' inheritance, who only know how to divide profits but cannot generate them, are nothing more than sleeping, eating, and excreting. Besides this, they do nothing all year round. Such people are superficially "people," but they hold a pig-life outlook. Isn't that lamentable?

The Legless Crab and the Seedless Date

— Zheng Yimei

These are two interesting stories that seem to be comparable, so I will now narrate them.

There was a man surnamed Xie who was a prefect in a certain province during the Qing Dynasty. He was extremely snobbish. His brother-in-law was a low-ranking official who came to the province to seek promotion. Xie looked down on his brother-in-law because his official position was too humble. One day, Xie invited many famous officials to admire chrysanthemums and drink wine. His brother-in-law thought this was a good opportunity to meet those important people and use it as a stepping stone for advancement. However, Xie strongly disapproved, fearing that the lowly rank would affect his own reputation. Somehow, his wife found out and complained to him. Xie had no choice but to invite his brother-in-law to attend. Unexpectedly, the brother-in-law's conversation was elegant, and his social skills were sophisticated, which earned him the praise of those famous officials. Xie was very jealous. Later, during the wine game of couplets, Xie used this to mock him, saying, "The kowtowing bug always stays beneath people." His brother-in-law was very quick-witted and immediately replied, "The legless crab should not flaunt its abilities." Xie's use of "legless" for the word "crab" was extremely clever.

During Zhang Changtui's era, a certain county magistrate surnamed Zhang in Shandong misappropriated tens of thousands of taels of public funds. He was a skilled flatterer. Previously, he had been a clerk in a certain office. One day, Zhang and the chief of the office went to the home of a director for a banquet. The director happened to bring out honey dates to serve the guests. The chief ate one and praised the date as seedless. He then picked one and gave it to Zhang. Zhang ate the date and found a seed, which he swallowed forcefully. The chief asked him how it was. Zhang said the date was seedless and a wonderful variety. The chief urged him to eat another, so he ate several in succession. The date seeds nearly blocked his throat. The chief asked the director where these dates came from and why they were seedless. The director said, "These are ordinary dates, how could they be seedless?" The chief looked at Zhang. Zhang said unnaturally, "There are sometimes seeds." The chief said, "Why haven't I seen you spit out any seeds?" Zhang was ashamed and had no reply. It became a laughingstock for a time.

Green Tangerines

— Zhu Yan

Occasionally, I glimpsed a few green tangerines on a hawker's fruit stall in the market. Their round, green, and shiny forms pierced my eyes, and then they stirred the strings of my broken heart.

In principle, these many unripe green tangerines should still be nurtured in the orchard: caressed by the sunlight, nourished by fertilizer, and irrigated with clean water! They shouldn't be displayed in the market for sale so early. But that cruel gardener, only seeking his own benefit, disregards whether you are ripe or not, tearing you raw from the branches, making you a tool for his own profit. Preventing you from ever having the chance to develop sweet juice.

Ah! My fate as a wanderer, isn't it the same as those unfortunate green tangerines? Overwhelming economic obstacles force young people who should still be pursuing further education in school to abandon their books midway, shatter their dreams, and sacrifice their future, entering society as beasts of burden with tears in their eyes. But his essence was originally immature, all he has is barrenness and astringency! From then on, he has no blessing to receive the warmth of the gentle sun, the cultivation of fertilizer and water. He will never turn into a moving golden color, brewing rich and sweet juice. He can only longingly envy his lucky companions, advancing towards the path of success, while he himself is forever foolish, impoverished, and astringent! The final result is nothing more than being abandoned on the side of the road.

Green tangerines! You suffer at the hands of a greedy gardener, being picked before your essence is ripe. I am trapped by the evil money, applying knowledge to the world before my knowledge is enriched. I deeply sympathize with you, pity you. Ah! You are the symbol of my destiny!

The Most Peculiar Will

This is the most peculiar will in the world. Decrease in Millionaires

In the Netherlands, the number of millionaires in 1931 decreased by 249 compared to last year. Whether the economic recession is affecting the Netherlands has become a question. Last year's statistics showed that the Netherlands had a total of 1,057 millionaires, but in 1931, there were 1,306. Their total assets have decreased from 2,931,000,000 yuan to 2,323,000,000 yuan. At the same time, the total salaries paid nationally have also decreased from 4,367,000弗路林 to 4,206,000,000弗路林. The total tax revenue in the Netherlands has also decreased from 15,623,000,000 to 14,300,000,000弗路林.

Brave Woman

A special express train, carrying many passengers and luggage, was traveling on the railway. The driver did not pay attention, but the bridge ahead had recently collapsed, and it would be dangerous to drive over it. However, he suddenly saw a red shawl spread on the railway, it was an Indian woman's garment, and several women stood at both ends of the shawl. So he pulled the emergency brakes several times, very urgently, but those women did not move at all, resulting in him having to stop the train. But the place where the train stopped was only a few yards away from the collapsed bridge. The incident occurred in Mumbai, India.

American Highways

In the United States, the length of plateau roads will soon reach three million miles. At the end of 1932, the length of plateau roads passable by automobiles was 875,000 miles, of which 275,000 miles were provincial roads. The total length of plateau roads in the United States is now 3,040,000 miles, of which 360,000 miles are provincial roads and 2,680,000 miles are national roads. Among the provincial roads, there are also 200,000 miles of interesting plateau roads.

New Pigeon Record

In Odessa, Russia, a homing pigeon flew home from afar, covering a distance of 1,300 miles. This pigeon was sold twice in Moscow and bought back home by a pigeon lover. Both times, it flew back home. According to the original owner, this pigeon has probably broken the world record.

Dog that Delivers Mail

A German dog, whose original owner is unknown. He has recently been guarding the post office door for his owner, Lines, who is an experienced postman. Every day, he carries letters and runs to Southern Sudan 波丹 twice. Years ago, this dog always followed him twice a day. But Lines recently reached the age limit and retired. However, this journey is an important thing in the dog's life. Therefore, although he explained the reason to the dog, the dog always guards the door of the post office, refusing to go with the new owner.

Banana Promotion

The propaganda of the German National Socialist Party is prohibited in Austria. However, a strange incident occurred here where bananas were used as propaganda items. After a ship of fresh fruit arrived in Vienna, it was distributed to merchants throughout the city. Who knew that every banana was printed with the Hitlerized symbol, which is forbidden in Austria. The police began to intervene. Although sales were still permitted, public display on fruit stalls was not allowed. They also took photos as evidence.

The Northeastern Four Company Commanders, Episode 19

— Zhang Henshui

Desiring to Leave and Then Desiring to Stay, Remembering the Past in the Same Carriage; Half-Crying and Half-Laughing, Leaning on a Pillow in the Sickly, 残秋

Guizhi admired the chrysanthemums for a while, feeling a chill on her body, and walked back into the house. Unexpectedly, at that time, she only cared about looking at the chrysanthemums and forgot that she was wearing a thin cloth jacket. After entering the room, when she went to find clothes to add to keep warm, she already felt a little tired. Gradually, her mind became dizzy, and she caught a cold. When a person is so upset that there is nothing they can do, they are very likely to want to sleep. Since she was feeling unwell, she might as well go to bed. She spread out the bedding, piled the pillow high, and leaned her body against it, only covering the lower half of her body with the quilt. Her face was half-turned, and her eyes slowly closed. Jiang was working in the outer room and didn't pay attention. For half a day, she didn't hear any movement from the inner room, and she thought to herself that this child's character has been changing a lot lately. Sometimes she stands in the yard in a daze, sometimes she sits alone in the room propping her head and thinking foolishly, sometimes she sighs to herself. She would say a word or two to herself. What is all this for? At this time, she hasn't made a sound for a long time, maybe she's having another one of her moods. Jiang thought like this and stretched her head and looked inside through the crack in the door curtain. Guizhi's face was facing the door, and she saw it through the crack in the curtain, just a face looking back. Only her cheeks were red, showing two large round blushes, and there were two lines of tears flowing down the sides of her eyes. Jiang was startled when she saw this situation. What wronged her that she started crying? (260)

Principal Xu of Beiping University Persistently Resigns

(Beiping, 5th) Principal Xu Yongming of Beiping University is very firm in his intention to resign.
