The Ministry of Education Makes Concessions on the Unified Examination Methods; Students Who Fail in One or Two Subjects Will Be Temporarily Allowed to Advance

The Ministry of Education, considering that various primary and secondary schools in various places have requested exemptions or modifications to the graduation examinations, has revised the regulations to make concessions based on the opinions of students and school authorities. The principles required for decision-making have been recorded in previous reports. Yesterday, according to the reporter of the Daily News, the graduation examinations were originally held to rectify the uneven levels of education. In recent years, the levels of secondary schools have varied the most, while primary schools are still relatively uniform. Looking at the results of this year's examinations, the Ministry has decided to change the method of calculating scores to accommodate the difficulties expressed by the school authorities. The proportions are as follows: graduation examination results account for 60%, and school graduation grades account for 40%. The graduation grades must be based on 60% for daily grades and 40% for graduation examinations. (2) Students who fail in three or more subjects will be required to repeat the grade. If they fail in one or two subjects, the examination committee will issue a certificate allowing them to advance temporarily. After passing the next examination, they will be given a diploma. Because holding make-up examinations in the same year for students who fail the graduation examination may hinder their entrance examinations, the make-up examination is abolished to facilitate advancement.

Rural Education Society Sets Date for Establishment; General Assembly to Be Held in Qixia Rural Teachers' School Next January

In recent years, my country's rural economy has been on the verge of bankruptcy. Tracing the source, it is due to the lack of knowledge among farmers and the failure to popularize education. Therefore, rural education is the only essential plan for developing the countryside. The Chinese Rural Education Society is organized by people in the country who are enthusiastic about rural education, with the aim of concentrating the strength of rural education colleagues across the country to jointly plan the development of the rural education movement. It has been approved and filed by the Central Party Department and the Ministry of Education. Details have been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday, the society held its second preparatory meeting at the Nanjing YMCA. Attendees included Zhang Zhiwen, Tang Qiyu, Zhao Hongqian, Sun Fang, He Yushu (represented by Xu Rong), Xiang Jutan (represented by Zhao Hongqian), Huang Zhifu, Peng Baichuan, etc. The Central Party Department also had instructor Zhang Jiao present. The meeting was chaired by Zhang Zhiwen and recorded by Peng Baichuan. The following key cases were resolved: (1) Deciding the date for the establishment congress. It was decided that the establishment congress would be held on January 27th (Saturday), 23rd year of Republic, at the Qixia Rural Teachers' School in Nanjing Qixia County, Jiangsu Province. The congress will last for two days. (2) Soliciting members. It was decided that (1) letters would be sent to normal schools and rural teachers' schools in various provinces inviting them to join the society as group members, (2) each member should introduce at least one new member, (3) how to divide and cooperate in the preparatory work for the establishment congress. It was decided that (1) sending meeting notices (collecting membership fees), reprinting the society's constitution, printing election ballots, and preparing for food, lodging, and reception will be handled by Huang Zhifu and Li Shaoliang, (2) drafting plans and organizing proposals will be handled by Zhang Zhiwen and Tang Qiyu, (3) raising funds will be handled by Sun Fang and Zhao Hongqian, (4) preparing official documents requesting the Central Party Department and the Ministries of Education and Interior to send personnel to the meeting for guidance, and requesting the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways to approve fare reductions for transportation will be handled by Peng Baichuan.

Development of Film and Drama in Polish Culture

A member of the China-Poland Cultural Association recently translated a detailed account of film and drama in Polish culture. Excerpts are provided below (the following is the translated text):

During the silent film era, the export of Polish films abroad was a rare occurrence. Only "The Tragedy of the Foreman" was screened in eight countries – Germany, Austria, Denmark, Sweden, Norway, Czechoslovakia, Romania, and the Netherlands – an exceptional case. Since the rise of sound films, the development of the Polish film industry abroad has been flourishing. Films like "The Orderly," "Ten Criminals and Two Musicians," "One Tenth of the Earth," "Hundred-Meter Love," and "For the Road" have been screened in countries such as Egypt, the United States, Belgium, Italy, Denmark, Sweden, France, Czechoslovakia, Romania, Yugoslavia, Chile, Palestine, Spain, Latvia, and Estonia. Furthermore, the sale of film copyrights abroad is also common. For instance, "The Protection of the Holy Mother" was sold to the United States for 30,000 yuan. The new film "The Echo of Peace" is being filmed in the Tatra Mountains. The recording equipment, invented and manufactured in Poland, is portable, doesn't require electricity, and can be installed in an ordinary car, similar in form to those produced by Fox and Western Electric. The creator and inventor is Mr. "Berniard." According to the American Film Yearbook, in 1932, the United States imported a total of 198 films, of which nine were Polish, accounting for 5% of American film imports. This is truly commendable and makes us lament that Chinese films, except for those watched by overseas Chinese, have not yet developed abroad. Poland recently held a "National Polish Book Promotion Week," promoting to the middle class, farmers, workers, intellectuals, and in schools and the military. The first item on the agenda was a film screening, followed by book exhibitions, lectures, and parades, demonstrating the wide use and significant impact of film. In Yugoslavia, Polish dramas will be staged this season, including "Accident" by Rosworski and "The Monik Affair" by Sikorska.

Additionally, "The Lawyer" and "Roses" by Renli Ininski are scheduled for performance. The Baerograd Opera House has decided to stage the opera "Helga" by Polish composer Monisko. A theater in Prague, the capital of the Czech Republic, is currently staging a play by a young Polish author titled "Female Doctor." The wife of the famous Czech playwright Shedechick is playing the lead role. The Warsaw National Theater commemorated the 100th anniversary of the first performance of "Revenge" by Count Freicher. This masterpiece by Freicher is still regarded by the Polish people as the ancestor of Polish drama, and the actors selected are all famous national stars, in celebration of this grand anniversary.

German, Austrian, and Swiss Alumni Association to Build Clubhouse

The executive committee of the Nanjing German, Austrian, and Swiss Alumni Association, including Zhu Jiahua, held a meeting in Nanjing today (the 6th) to discuss the construction of a clubhouse and other important matters.

Zhongshan Cultural and Educational Center to Edit Series of Doctrines – 50 Titles to be Completed in Two Years

The Zhongshan Cultural and Educational Center of this city, in order to promote the Three Principles of the People and enrich teaching materials on party doctrines, is editing a series of 50 doctrines to be completed in two years. The manuscript rules and the first batch of book titles (25 titles) are listed below: (1) Eligibility for Submission: Submitters are limited to current civic teachers (formerly known as party doctrine teachers) and deans of discipline at all levels of schools. (2) Application Procedures: A. Before the end of January 1934, applicants must first register at this center at 803 Foch Road, Shanghai, providing detailed information including their name, age, place of origin, gender, education, school name, position, party membership card (date and number), and party doctrine teacher certification (date and number), as well as the proposed book title, editing principles, table of contents, and bibliography. B. After the Party Doctrine Series Review Committee of this center approves the editing principles and table of contents submitted by the applicant, an official letter of appointment will be issued (applicants who fail the review will be notified separately). (3) Word Count: Each book should be approximately 20,000 to 25,000 words. (4) Style: Primarily in vernacular Chinese. (5) Manuscript Fee: Five silver dollars per thousand words. (6) Book Titles: A Brief History of Revolutions in Various Countries, Nation and State, Colonies and Semi-Colonies, An Overview of the Aggression of Powers Against China, The Five-Power Constitution, A Short History of Civil Rights Movements in Various Countries, All-People Politics, Tutelage and Constitutional Government, The Principle of People's Livelihood and Communism, The Principle of People's Livelihood and Socialism, The Principle of People's Livelihood and Capitalism, Labor-Capital Cooperation, Cooperative Movements in Various Countries, Psychological Construction, Industrial Community Planning, Regulation of Capital, Equalization of Land Ownership, An Overview of Chinese Agriculture, An Overview of Chinese Industry, Chinese Famine, Rural Relief Programs, The Chinese Grain Problem, The Silk and Cotton Industries, Government of the People, by the People, for the People.

Training Supervisory Department Intensifies National Military Training – City Committee Established, Actively Preparing and Proceeding – Scheduled to Convene Meetings of Military Instructors from Various Schools

The National Military Training Committee has been organized and established, with four provinces including Hunan, Jiangxi, and Jiangsu. The city's military training was also officially established on the 20th of last month at the old Shanghai County Office on Penglai Road, and has notified various schools accordingly. In the future, regarding the guidelines for national military training and practical training methods, meetings of military training instructors from various schools will be convened to discuss and respond to environmental needs. The details are recorded as follows:

Organization of the Committee

According to the organizational regulations, the National Military Training Committee is directly supervised by the Training Supervisory Department and the Ministry of Education. Each province and city in the country has established a committee to engage in unified training. The city's military training committee was established on the 20th of last month, with five members. The chairman is He Chongti, and the full-time member is Wang Jingyi (both appointed by the Training Supervisory Department). The members Chen Bai and Du Gang (both appointed by the City Education Bureau) and Chen Zhiyi (appointed by the City Security Office) have also assumed their positions and are engaged in planning all military training matters in the city. All military training instructors in the city, who were previously under the direct command and supervision of the Training Supervisory Department, are now also transferred to this committee for unified management.

Distribution of Committee Funds

According to a discussion with Wang Jingyi, a full-time member of the city's military training committee, the salaries of the committee members are still paid separately by their original agencies. The salaries of the committee's staff and office expenses amount to approximately 400 yuan per month, which is allocated from the City Education Bureau's education funds. The salaries of the instructors at each school are still paid from the school's funds.

Convening Instructor Meetings

Wang also stated that since the committee was newly established, everything is in the initial stages. It is currently difficult to implement comprehensive training for all levels in the city's national military training. For now, training will be intensified in high schools and above, and other vocational groups will be planned within a possible scope. The implementation of military training is now scheduled to take place between the 10th and 12th of this month, convening a meeting of military training instructors from high schools and above in the city to determine the guidelines for military training and detailed regulations for various items that should be noted in the future.

Notification to Various Schools After Establishment

After the establishment of the committee, an official letter was sent to various schools in the city, stating: "Respectfully, according to the instruction No. 1320 of the Training Supervisory Department, it is ordered that the Shanghai Municipal National Military Training Committee should be established in accordance with the regulations to facilitate training. It has been submitted to the Military Commission for approval in accordance with Article 2 of the Provisional Regulations of the National Military Training Committee of each province and city, appointing He Chongti as the Colonel Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal National Military Training Committee, and transferring Wang Jingyi, the Lieutenant Colonel full-time member of the Fujian National Military Training Committee, to be the Lieutenant Colonel full-time member of the committee. In addition to separate orders, the Provisional Regulations and Detailed Rules of Procedure are enclosed, ordering the members to comply, proceed to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau to discuss the rapid organization and establishment, and report back. This order, etc., in accordance with Article 2 of the Provisional Regulations of the National Military Training Committee of each province and city, Chen Bai and Du Gang are appointed by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, and Chen Zhiyi is appointed by the Shanghai Municipal Security Office as part-time members of our committee. It has been organized and located at the old silk office on Penglai Road in the South City. It was established yesterday, and an oath will be taken on another date. In addition to separate reports and orders, it is hereby notified for your information."

City Education Bureau Orders Schools to Register Publications

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to private schools at all levels in the city yesterday, stating: "It has been found that all school publications were previously ordered by this bureau to be submitted for review. Most of those submitted by various schools for review have not been registered, which is inconsistent with the publication law. The aforementioned publications are divided into two types: periodic and temporary. For periodic publications, in addition to submitting them to the Fourth Section of this bureau for record each period, they should first obtain a registration form from the municipal government in accordance with Article 7 of the Publication Law, attach the publication, fill it out in accordance with the form, and apply for registration. Afterwards, they should continue to report and submit them for review on a regular basis. For temporary publications, they should still be handled in accordance with the previous order. In addition to separate distribution, this order is hereby issued for your school to comply with."

(1) Public schools should adopt teaching materials on international knowledge and give extracurricular lectures. (2) Libraries should exhibit books on international knowledge for the general public to read. (3) Public education centers should hold exhibitions related to international knowledge. (4) Popular lecture halls should pay attention to this knowledge when giving lectures. (5) Compiling popular reading materials should focus on materials related to international knowledge. (6) Founding daily newspapers for the general public to read should publish as much international news as possible, etc. In this autumn of encirclement by powers, instilling the public with international knowledge is essential. After the training period, they will serve in the 22-story building of the association and receive generous subsidies. At present, there are already 40 to 50 applicants. It is also reported that the Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center has recently been entrusted by a factory to recruit several apprentices with elementary school degrees and poor families. It is advisable for those who have studied carpentry to apply.

Special Article

Progress of the Chinese Painting Exhibition in Paris (5)

At 3 PM on May 10th, the opening ceremony of the Chinese Art Exhibition was held at the Musée du Jeu de Paume. First, our Minister to France, Mr. Gu, and the French Minister of Education, Mr. Monzie, jointly issued invitations, inviting all sectors of French society to participate in this grand event. On that day, among those present from our country were Minister Gu and his wife, Counselor Xiao, Secretary Xie, Consul General Li, representatives from the Sino-French Industrial and Commercial Bank, Chinese representative Liu Fucheng, and the organizers of the painting exhibition, including Xu Beihong, Zhang Fengju, and Liu Hou, as well as more than 200 male and female students. From France, there were the Minister of Education, the Undersecretary of Fine Arts, the directors of various museums, art inspectors, celebrities from all walks of life, newspaper reporters, and more than 2,000 artists, creating a lively and grand atmosphere, perhaps an unprecedented promotional event for the Chinese in France. The opening ceremony was very simple, with the organizers leading Minister Gu, Minister Monzie, and the attendees on a tour of the exhibition for about two hours before it concluded. They all praised the exhibition and expressed their admiration. Newspaper reporters scrambled to take photos, and flashes of light dazzled the eyes. The months of hard work that had gone into the exhibition seemed to vanish into thin air at that moment.

After the opening of the painting exhibition, the number of visitors was extremely high. The entrance fee was five francs per person, and more than 25,000 people purchased tickets. Chinese students and personnel from French art and education institutions were admitted free of charge. The exhibition catalog was sold for ten francs per copy, with a total of 3,000 copies sold. Therefore, the total revenue from tickets and catalogs was more than 120,000 francs. In 1929, the Japanese government also held a Japanese painting exhibition at the Musée du Jeu de Paume, but its revenue was only 100,000 francs. This time, our Chinese painting exhibition earned one-fifth more, and this was during a time of global economic panic, so the achievement is truly remarkable. However, the amount of revenue has nothing to do with us, as the museum was borrowed, and all revenue belongs to the French national treasury. All that we gain is the praise of the audience and the acclaim of the newspapers. At a time when our country is beset by internal and external troubles and the Japanese are spending heavily to buy public opinion and spread slanderous articles about the Chinese, this painting exhibition has made a positive impression on the general public, prompting them to say good things about us, which is of some small benefit to our nation.

The exhibition was originally scheduled to last for one month, but at the request of the audience, it was extended twice, for a total of 45 days. During this period, there were more than 200 articles in newspapers from various countries criticizing the painting exhibition, in English, Russian, German, Italian, and French. To save space and avoid repetition, we have selected and translated more than ten articles as a general overview. In addition, there are comments on the painting exhibition from other foreign newspapers.

Le Temps (May 12) published an article by Millet, which stated, "The survival of China is like the growth of a living being, which must suffer pain before it can develop. Therefore, its internal strife, famine, and invasion by others are precisely the stimulants for its thinkers, mystics, and artists. This has always been the case throughout history. Looking at the organization of its art exhibition, it is even harder for us to believe that this moving China has reached its final breath. In the midst of national difficulties, organizing a Chinese painting exhibition is an extremely difficult task, but Professor Xu Beihong of National Central University and Liu Hou of the Sino-French University were able to accomplish it swiftly. Such activities can only be achieved by a nation that can preserve its inherent spirit for generations."

Paris Weekly (May 12) published an article by Lu Haituo, which stated, "China is currently in a difficult period and cannot transport its ancient masterpieces to France, but its lively and attention-grabbing modern painting exhibition is already worthy of our admiration. The various styles and trends of Chinese painting are all represented here by works of extremely high value. (Omission) We should pay special respect to the modern works brought by Professor Xu Beihong of Central University. Mr. Xu is currently the most famous painter in China. We also cannot help but especially praise Gao Qifeng's sailing boat, Wang Yiting's fierce Da Hou, Chen Shuren, a member of the Central Committee of the Kuomintang, waterfall, and his peach blossom belt which makes one feel a sense of flow, Pan Tianshou's flower-carrying, and Ye Jiying's Lushan scenery. However, there are many such works, and we cannot help but forgive ourselves for not being able to mention them all in detail. (Omission)"

Free Talk

The Negro Question

— Xu Maoyong

Reading the recent newspapers makes me believe that there are extremely honest individuals among the news editors of Shanghai. For example, consider the following news item:

"Reuters, Baltimore, USA, 28th: On October 18th, a lynching of a Negro occurred in Maryland, USA. The governor sent a team of soldiers to the scene of the incident last night to arrest nine key suspects. However, local officials made excuses and delayed the process, resulting in the army only arresting three people. The difficulty of punishing lynchers in the United States is evident from this."

This is a common occurrence, but some newspapers have added headlines like "Lynching in the United States Too?" This implies that the United States is a civilized country and should not have lynching.

This is due to an overreliance on the superficial beauty of the term "civilized country." If we follow this logic, not only should lynching disappear, but discrimination against Negroes should also have ceased long ago. In the above news item, the persecution of Negroes is actually more significant than the act of lynching itself.

But this is not surprising either. In 1776, the United States declared the equality and freedom of all people, and in 1863, President Lincoln issued the Emancipation Proclamation. However, these were all beautiful lies, and Negroes have yet to receive fair treatment. According to the so-called Jim Crow Laws in the southern states of the United States, special areas are designated in the back of streetcars and buses for Negroes to sit in. Even in schools and waiting rooms at parking lots, Negroes are not allowed to mix with whites. In theaters, Negroes who intrude into white seating areas are often subjected to "lynching."

Lynching Negroes is not considered a crime or a disgrace. American newspapers often publish such news with large headlines. The most brutal forms of lynching even involve piling up firewood and burning Negroes alive.

But neither these Negroes nor the Jews will disappear under the cruelty and oppression of civilized races. On the contrary, even the most compliant and gentle Negroes have developed racial and class consciousness and are waking up. Even white people themselves have realized that relying solely on "terror" tactics cannot prevent this race from ever rising again. Siegfried said, "Neither southward nor northward can we find a solution to this problem. The race problem plunges us into an abyss of terror." (America Comes of Age) According to one group of people, the problem can be solved only if Negroes make greater progress in society, white people can reflect, and then the two can move towards coexistence and co-prosperity.

But according to Scott Nearing, the liberation of Negroes in America can only be achieved if Negro working masses join hands and build a new social organization together.

Which view is correct, right and wrong, we can only wait for future events to prove.

The Author of *Water Margin*

— Yu Shixia

The author of *Water Margin* is traditionally believed to be Shi Nai'an.

Shi Nai'an is a controversial figure. In Ming Dynasty scholar Lang Ying's *Qixiu Leigao*, *Water Margin* is attributed to Song Jiang and said to be compiled by Luo Ben Guanzhong of Hangzhou, but also mentioned as a version by Shi Nai'an of Qiantang. Gao Ru's *Baichuan Shuzhi* lists a hundred-chapter *Zhongyi Shuihu Zhuan*, also saying it's a version by Shi Nai'an of Qiantang, compiled and arranged by Luo Guanzhong. Li Zhuowu's preface to *Zhongyi Shuihu Zhuan* states that *Water Margin* is a work of passion by the two gentlemen, Shi and Luo. Only Wang Qi's *Xu Wenxian Tongkao* includes *Water Margin* in the classics, attributed solely to Luo Guanzhong. The *Water Margin* editions seen today from the Ming dynasty sometimes don't mention an author, sometimes credit Shi Nai'an as the editor, and sometimes say it was compiled by Shi Nai'an and edited by Luo Guanzhong. It's clear that people in the Ming Dynasty were already confused about whether the book was written by Shi Nai'an, Luo Guanzhong, or a collaboration.

Zhou Liangong's *Yinshuwu Shuying* says, "Tradition holds that *Water Margin* was written by Luo Guanzhong of Yue, in the early Hongwu period, or by Shi Nai'an of the Yuan Dynasty... Recently, Jin Shengtan, after the seventieth chapter, determined that it was continued by Luo Guanzhong, vehemently criticizing Luo, and falsely created a preface by Shi before, thus the book became Shi's." It's evident that crediting Shi Nai'an as the author of *Water Margin* was confirmed by Jin Shengtan around the Ming-Qing transition, and he also determined that the latter part of the *Water Margin* was continued by Luo Guanzhong. The modern scholar Wu Mei, in *Guqu Chentan*, said that "*Yougui* was written by Shi Junmei, whose given name was Hui, also known as the Layman Nai'an, who wrote *Water Margin*." He asserts that Shi Nai'an was also a playwright, but his basis is unknown. When Hu Shih wrote *Textual Research on Water Margin*, he said that Shi Nai'an was probably a fictitious character like "Mr. Uyou" or "Lord Wangshigong," merely a hypothetical name. This truly confuses us!

About a year ago, I saw an article in a newspaper supplement by Hu Ruiting called "Textual Research on Shi Nai'an's Ancestry," which seemed to confirm that Shi Nai'an was a real person. He said, "While conducting official household registration surveys, traversing long distances, and registering households, in Baicou Town, Dongtai County, there was a Shi Family Bridge. I saw in their ancestral hall the fifteenth generation ancestor whose personal name was Nai'an, and I secretly suspected him. Inquiring of his descendants, I learned that he was indeed Shi Nai'an, the author of *Water Margin*. Further, I requested to view the genealogy and obtained a brief history of Nai'an, as well as fragmented epitaphs." The brief history of Nai'an and the epitaphs will not be recorded here. According to this, *Water Margin* was indeed written by Shi Nai'an, and Shi Nai'an was indeed a real person. Even now, there is a genealogy to verify and descendants to inquire from. If the "Saint" Hu, who claims to have a penchant for textual research and history, were to see this news, wouldn't it be a joyful event?

If Hu Ruiting's article doesn't lie, and there is indeed a Shi family genealogy in Dongtai that can be verified and is reliable, then the case of Shi Nai'an, which has been a mystery since the Ming and Qing dynasties, can be resolved. First, we know that Shi Nai'an's given name was Zian, that he was from Huai'an at the end of the Yuan Dynasty, and that he once served as an official in Qiantang but left due to dissatisfaction. He personally witnessed Zhang Shicheng's uprising. He died when Shicheng failed, at the age of seventy-five. His birth and death were approximately between 1290 and 1365 AD. Second, Shi Nai'an's works are not limited to *Water Margin*. There are also *Zhi Yu*, *Romance of the Three Kingdoms*, *Sui Tang Zhizhuan*, and *San Sui Ping Yao Zhuan*. Luo Guanzhong was indeed a disciple of Shi Nai'an and assisted Nai'an with his writing.

Thoughts on Watching the Haijingbo Circus

— Ye Yongzhen

1. The Elephant's Handstand

Because I am a commoner in a chaotic world, I want to see a little more of the things in front of me. So I bought a six-mao ticket and went into the Haijingbo Circus to watch a circus performance.

The opening act was a display of skills by Indian giant elephants. Five elephants, their heads decorated with bright, metallic trinkets, clanging and tinkling, followed a trainer into the arena, first circling around it.

The elephants walked in perfect step. I'm not paying attention to others; as for me, I had never seen elephants perform tricks, so I watched very carefully, with a touch of curiosity.

After that circle was completed, the trainer cracked the whip in his hand on the ground, and the five elephants all stopped in their places.

The first trick was for each elephant to raise its front two feet, while the other two feet behind remained prostrate. They did this very skillfully, as if they were used to it.

Then, the people watching in the arena laughed.

Because of this laughter, I don't know if they understood the people's compliments or felt the trainer's cues, but these five elephants, standing upright, moved their front legs up and down like bowing, and turned another circle in place.

Naturally, the people laughed even more. This time, the people themselves received the elephants' compliments.

Thus, what followed was the elephant pyramid. One elephant was curling two flags of "Blue Sky, White Sun, and a Wholly Red Earth" with its trunk, while the other four stood on both sides. The elephants in the back rested their front legs on the backs of the elephants in front, and their trunks were all curled up high.

The people laughed even louder, and some were clapping. This time, it wasn't just us yellow-faced people who benefited from the elephants' compliments, but the country as well. Needless to say, this is a dignified thing!

However, I myself felt that I had only laughed once, and that was at the end, when these five elephants performed handstands.

Imagine such corpulent animals, resting their front legs on the ground and desperately lifting their hind legs into the air to please people; how much is that effort worth people's sympathy, and how much is that situation worth people's amusement!

So I couldn't help but laugh.

The performances of these five Indian giant elephants ended there. The metallic trinkets on their heads continued to ring, and they listened to the trainer's instructions and happily walked back to the "menagerie" in perfect step.

So I couldn't help but feel something:

In the Himalayas, the Karakoram Mountains, the Hindu Kush, the Suleiman Mountains, the Ghats of India, there are vast forests where these elephants could live and be raised, leaning against craggy rocks above and overlooking streams below. Wouldn't it be better for these elephants to live there and enjoy their lives without having to do so many performances? Why must they follow people, listen to the whip in their hands, and do so many sets of difficult things, only to seek their own livelihood and expose their various shortcomings? What good does this ultimately do for them? Does it mean that their freedom can be exchanged for a few shiny metal trinkets on their heads and a burst of laughter from the audience?

I think no one would think that way, if the elephants were a little smarter.

However, it is said that although elephants are the most enormous animals, they are also the most docile animals, and it is also said that the reason elephants are captured by humans is that there is first an internal traitor who lures their own kind to jointly enjoy this fate of hardship - then, if I think like that, I feel a little uneasy for myself.

Isn't it said that our nation is also the most enormous, the most docile, and the most prone to produce internal traitors?

Then everything can be predicted, can't it, everyone?

Two Brothers (50)

— By Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

It was especially his father that struck him with alarm. Was this soft, content, and foolishly beaming fat man, Jean's father? No, no, Jean was not like him at all.

His family! For the past two days, a foreign and sinister hand, the hand of a dead man, had been pulling up and destroying all the ties binding these four people together, one by one. Now it was all over, everything had been destroyed. He no longer had a mother, because he could no longer love her, he could no longer respect her with that tenderness and absolute reverence that sons must have in their hearts. He no longer had a brother, because this brother of his was the son of a stranger. All that was left to him was a father, only this fat man, and this fat man, he did not love at all.

Suddenly he said:

"Hey, Mom, have you found that portrait?"

She stared at him in surprise:

"What portrait?"

"The portrait of Maraîsa."

"No, I haven't looked for it, but I think I can find it."

"What are you talking about?" Roland asked.

Pierre said to him:

"A portrait of Maraîsa that used to be in the living room when we lived in Paris. I thought Jean would be happy to have it."

Roland exclaimed:

"That's right, that's right, I remember it perfectly; and I even saw that portrait at the end of last week. When your mother was sorting out papers, she took it out of the desk. It was Thursday or Friday. Do you remember, Eglantine? At the time, I was shaving, and you took the portrait out of a drawer and placed it with a pile of letters on a chair next to you, and you burned half of that pile of letters, didn't you? Just two or three days before Jean received his inheritance, you touched that portrait, isn't that strange? If I believed in feelings, I would say that was one of those premonitions!"

Madame Roland replied calmly:

"Yes, that's right, I know where that portrait is; I'll go and find it."

So she had lied! Just this morning, when her son asked her where that portrait had gone, she had lied in her answer: "I don't remember very well... maybe it's in my writing desk."

A few days before, she had seen, read, touched, and looked at this painting, and then she had hidden it in that secret drawer, with some letters, with her private letters.

Pierre looked at his lying mother. He looked at her with the fury of a son who had been deceived, robbed of sacred love, he looked at her with the jealousy of a man who had been blind for a long time and had finally discovered a shameful affair. If he had been the woman's husband, he would have grabbed her wrist, grabbed her shoulders or grabbed her hair, thrown her to the ground, beat her, kicked her, trampled on her! But now he couldn't say anything, couldn't do anything, couldn't express anything, couldn't expose anything. He was her son, he had no revenge to take, he had not been wronged.

Silk Market Still Unimproved Overseas

Wuxi Cocoon Floss Transported to Shanghai for Sale: As the end of the year approaches, the silk cocoons stored in Wuxi need to be transported to Shanghai for sale. Yesterday, the Shanghai-Nanjing train transported 84 pieces of cocoon floss from Wuxi to Shanghai, awaiting sale on the market.

Yesterday, the Sichuan-Hankou merchants imported 30 cases of Golden Deer, Golden Bell, and other brands of this month's futures, priced at 175 yuan to 161 yuan and 75 cents net.

Foreign Firms' Silk Sales Still Lack Improvement: Although the strike in American silk weaving factories has been resolved, their silk inventories are very large, enough to meet demand for the next month or two. Moreover, Japanese silk is being sold at low prices relentlessly, making it difficult for Chinese silk sales to improve in the short term. Yesterday, only the French firm imported 10 bales of yellow factory silk, and the Indian firm imported 12 bales of yellow coarse silk, with prices remaining stable.

Commentary

Appeasing Students Studying in Japan

— Wei Ba

Recently, Gan Jielan, the military attache of the Chinese embassy in Japan, stated that "abuse by Japanese dormitories and lodging industries has aroused resentment among students studying in Japan." Subsequently, the Cultural Affairs Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is striving to improve treatment in order to appease students studying in Japan, expecting them to become important figures in China when they return home in the future. If they do not have good intentions beforehand, they will inevitably loudly oppose Japan once they return to China, which will have a significant impact on Sino-Japanese friendship.

Japan's policy of aggression can be described as meticulous. They take what others discard, and we cannot help but admire their unique vision, appreciating this group of future "important figures in China" and "preparing in advance."

"Using barbarians to control barbarians" has been China's traditional diplomatic policy. Therefore, when Eastern powers invade, they quickly import Western powers as a counterbalance. Originally, the intention was to use "Barbarian A" to control "Barbarian B," not to use "A among Barbarian A" to control "B among Barbarian A." However, this trick has been learned by the Eastern neighbor, who is even more skilled in using the strategy of "using Chinese to control Chinese."

Supporting Warlord A to overthrow Warlord B, and then supporting Warlord B to overthrow Warlord A, has been the essence of Japan's diplomacy towards China for the past twenty years. For the success of this diplomatic policy, they must find henchmen among the students studying in Japan. Therefore, they make every effort to promote and create various terms such as "pro-Japanese faction," "pro-American faction," and "pro-Russian faction" in the hope of using the old trick of subjugating Korea to divide the Chinese people. They also implement a kind of anesthetic education for general students studying in Japan. This has been effective, and the creation of "Manchukuo" is a perfect example.

Since Japan created the so-called "Manchukuo," it has been using many students studying in Japan and well-known scholars as its henchmen everywhere. The "Manchukuo" Ministry of Education and the Education Bureau have organizations such as the "Royal Way Lecture Society" and the "Disaster Area慰慰团" [sic, probably 宣慰團, comfort group], and the members are mostly these students and scholars. The Japanese know very well the psychology of the villagers who worship foreign students, so they use their mouths to spread smoke bombs to the public, lecturing on absurd words such as "The True Lord is reborn, the Royal Way is revived, Manchuria and Japan are friendly, and the people live in peace and prosperity." Every time the Japanese puppet army massacres righteous soldiers or loots a village, they always bring out this group of people to lecture for a while, so that the people do not oppose the actions of the friendly army (Japanese army), so as to save them to the paradise of the Royal Way. (See the Education in the Northeast after the Incident in the 48th issue of the 8th volume of the Life Weekly) How can 30 million people be ruled by 10 to 20 thousand Japanese troops? It all depends on these henchmen. The education that the Japanese have given to Chinese students studying in Japan has not been in vain, but our study abroad has been entirely run by the Japanese.

Originally, the reason for studying abroad was admiration and learning for one's own reference, but the result was that some people were "left behind by the 'learning'," which is truly a strange thing. What I don't understand is that people are generally called animals with emotions and reason, but why are Chinese people so docile and able to receive Japanese education to "meet expectations"? I am afraid that it is not a "bitter life" destined, but a "slave life" destined?

Restoration

— Guang Han

The twentieth century does not count as ours, because China in 1933, on the surface, seems to be working hard to "run forward" with others, and even shouting "catch up"; in reality, it is desperately "driving backward," "turning around," and everything presents a "restoration" scene!

First, after the May Fourth Movement, the "New Culture Movement has not yet succeeded," and the thread-bound "classics" that were just "shelved" have been encouraged to be read again. It is said that the classics are China's only "treasure book" (half a book of Confucius can govern the world), and all of China's current academic fields have been differentiated from it: "When drinking water, think of the source," how can we "discard it like a worn shoe"? Therefore, "people with intentions" have "worked hard" and "vigorously promoted it." From then on, "the spirit remains in the Lu Temple," and "our way will not decline"!

Secondly, the "imperial examination system," which was recognized as harmful to scholars and overthrown, has now been "revived" with the shells of "general examinations" and "higher examinations." The only difference is that what was tested before was the "national eight-legged essay," and what is tested today is the "foreign eight-legged essay." As for the "new top scholars" who are "named on the gold list" after the "palace examination," although they are not fortunate enough to receive the favor of the "Empress Dowager" personally pinning flowers; it is considered extremely honorable that "important figures" attend the ceremony to award certificates in person - moreover, although the streets have not been paraded as usual, it is certain that they will not use "horse riding" or "carriage riding," but will change to "motorcycle." In addition, the "unified examination" for primary and secondary schools, which was "vigorously and swiftly" implemented for a while, has also "emerged in response to the times." It can be seen that the "new imperial examination system" is even more prosperous today than in the past!

Thirdly, novels of the "gods and monsters" and "martial arts" genres have been strictly prohibited in "repeated orders"; even the films made by "Burning Big Hero" and others "to practice the mission of social education" have also suffered; but the countless "martial arts heroes" who have been abandoned, who have fought the "Eighteen Bronze Men Array," and who have been hidden in deep mountain temples for a long time, and the "jianghu heroes" who possess the unique skills of "flying over eaves and walking on walls," are fortunate enough to be able to raise their eyebrows and show their skills thanks to the "national examination"; and the "national martial arts," which has been passed down for thousands of years, has been able to avoid being buried. It is precisely "Heaven has not abandoned this martial art!" "We" take scholars through examinations" and "swing the stage to select heroes" at the same time; both literary and military skills are valued, which can be called a good plan. Unfortunately, no one has been able to pass the higher examination and be selected in the national examination at the same time; otherwise, the "literary and martial arts top scholar" who has both literary and martial arts stars descending on one person will be seen again in today's world!

The above are the major events, and there are still many to be listed! However, today's "restoration" in China only restores "half" of it, not "all" of it. For example, although ancient books must be studied in schools, natural sciences and social sciences must also be read; national martial arts should be enthusiastically promoted, and gunpowder, cannons, and airplanes must still be prepared.

Moreover, there are also opposite examples, which are very "trendy." That is the unspeakable, typical "as instructed" official document, which is said will be changed to colloquial language in the future, and even the addition of new-style punctuation and symbols is being implemented. This miracle is considered "rare and valuable" in our "ancient" and huge country. Who knows that there is a gentleman who is not content and sighs as if saying: "The promotion of colloquial language has been more than ten years old now, and as a result, only a few punctuation marks and symbols have been occupied in six-character notices and official documents, and there is a large group of people who are furious and indignant. I really don't know when the complete elimination of the feudal system will be."

Restoration is not necessarily a bad phenomenon. "Things will turn when they reach their extreme." Chinese culture may have now progressed to the highest degree, and restoration is a "necessary trend." Because "restoration" is "reversal." I remember the British old man Bernard Shaw ridiculed us, saying, "China has no culture"; this is simply a lie!

Relying on Connections

— Xu Cun

Mr. Zhou, the clerk, put on a stern face and said to him, "You really don't understand things. Last time you came, you brought a letter from Secretary Zhu. If there was something to do, wouldn't I have kept you? Would I have asked you to leave?"

He stood there respectfully. For every sentence Mr. Zhou said, he responded with "yes." He waited until he had finished speaking, and then bowed and said with a smile to the clerk Zhou, "What you said is absolutely right! But I am really too miserable. I can't stand not having anything to do for so long. So when I went back last time, I went to find Mrs. Wu, the director of the bank. Because she is from my hometown, and Mr. Wu has a wide circle of friends. I wanted to ask her to find something else for me to do. When I went, Mrs. Wu happened to be at home. I told her what I meant. She said that Secretary Zhu's letters are not very reliable. Because he writes too many letters of recommendation. Even if there are good positions, he has his own close people to arrange for. She said that there must still be vacancies here. But according to the rules, some have to be reserved for the people in high positions. Since you are in a hurry to find something to do, and you can't find anything else for the time being, I have to write a letter myself. You take this letter and go ask Mr. Zhou. Ask him not to make things difficult for you, and just say that I said so. I will say hello to Mr. Wu when he comes. This is her letter. I still ask you to give me a little work to do for Mrs. Wu's sake. As long as I can get by, I will no longer bother you repeatedly!" As he said this, he took out a letter from his body and presented it to Mr. Zhou with both hands.

He stood there bowing respectfully, watching Mr. Zhou's expression.

Mr. Zhou took the letter and read it. After reading it, he paused slightly, frowned, and said to him gently, "There really is no work anymore. Who doesn't have relatives and friends they know? You think! But since there is a letter from the director's wife, you can stay temporarily and do some odd jobs here for me. I will find a way for you to fill a formal position in the future."

Hearing this, he was as happy as a criminal hearing a pardon. From then on, he helped the original servant in the general affairs office, doing sweeping, fetching water, pouring tea, turning on the lights, and all kinds of chores. He did everything carefully. Mr. Shen, who worked with Mr. Zhou, also often praised him.

One evening, Mr. Zhou asked him to call Ah Fu, who was in charge of the reception room. Mr. Zhou said to Ah Fu with anger on his face, "I know you don't care whether you do it or not. Look at the reception room you are in charge of. I don't know how many days the floor hasn't been swept. The lights are on all night. You don't care about appearances, and you don't care about wasting resources. Do you want to go back to your hometown? Pack your bags as soon as possible and leave here tonight. Once..." Ah Fu was baffled when he heard this. He was stunned for a long time. Should he argue? It's not good to offend his superior! If he doesn't argue, he has a belly full of grievances that he can't tell! He had no choice but to suppress his anger and slowly replied, "I sweep the floor every day. You can investigate if you don't believe me. If I really don't sweep, you can punish me! As for the lights, Mr. Shen said that the other rooms are lit, and that room is dark, which is not very good. So he told me to turn them on. You can ask him if you don't believe me."

"Yes, I know you are very good at explaining. But now it's useless to be able to explain. Don't be long-winded. Hurry up and pack your bags and come back to settle your wages."

Ah Fu had no choice but to leave.

After a while, Mr. Shen walked in hurriedly. He asked Mr. Zhou, "I heard that you are going to fire Ah Fu? Ah Fu almost cried when he saw me and asked me to intercede for him. It was indeed me who told him to turn on the lights. I don't think there is anything else wrong. Why don't you forgive him for the first time? What do you think?"

"Old Li, you don't know. These people rely on their seniority and their big connections. If I don't give them some fear, it will be difficult to do things in the future. — Saying this, he lowered his voice again. — Moreover, the one who was recommended by the director's wife is also idle and has nothing to do."

Mr. Shen nodded silently.

From then on, he was in charge of the reception room, doing the things that Ah Fu used to do.

A Mother's Lesson

— Hu Ziju

"Lin'er, why did you sneak out to the road alone again today?" Lin'er's mother, a middle-aged woman of eleven years - holding the little hand of Lin'er, a child of seven or eight years old who had just strolled back from outside the alley gate - asked.

"Because it's very lively there, and there's a monkey show," Wang Yi, a calligrapher and painter of modern celebrities, originally from Changzhou

Lin'er replied, "So I went out to see it. Mom, that monkey is really smart! It can dress itself and wear a hat!" Lin'er, whose childishness had not faded, still deeply remembered the fun of the monkey he had just seen outside the alley gate. He simply did not hear his mother's question.

"Haven't I been telling you every day that children shouldn't run to the road alone without their parents' permission?" Lin'er's mother asked, chasing after the question because her question had not yet been understood by Lin'er.

"Mom, are you saying: there is a foreigner with a full face of beard and a yellow cloth wrapped on his head standing on the road over there?" Lin'er asked his mother with some understanding.

"Yes, he likes to catch children the most!" Mom said.

"I also know that," Lin'er said, "He wants to catch us Chinese children and make medicine!"

"I have other things I told you! Do you remember?"

"I remember them all in my heart." Lin'er nodded and said, "Those white-faced, blue-eyed foreigners running around on the road, they all want to catch our Chinese children too. Mom, is that right?"

"Then why did you sneak out to the road alone again today?"

"I have never been to the road!" Lin'er replied eagerly, "I just watched a monkey show at the alley gate. Later, I unintentionally saw a white-faced, blue-eyed foreigner not far from our alley gate, hitting a rickshaw puller with a stick. The rickshaw puller kept kowtowing to him. I was also afraid of being caught by that foreigner, so I ran back home in a hurry."

"Isn't that right? Those foreigners will hit adults with sticks when they see them, and they will catch those children to make medicine. Lin'er, think about it, how terrible is that?"

"It's extremely terrible!" Lin'er was stunned.

"Then will you dare to run out to the alley gate alone to play next time?" Lin'er's mother, knowing that her lecture this time had achieved considerable results, was very happy in her heart, and asked Lin'er further.

"Mom, I will definitely not dare to run out to the alley gate alone to wander around next time." Lin'er's small mouth finally uttered these words. Then a smile of victory could not help but appear on Lin'er's mother's cheeks.

"Processing and Rushing to Build" People

— Wen

The "God of Peace" has long been suffering from an incurable disease in Geneva and is approaching its death, but war is overlooking the two sides of Europe and the Pacific, making a hideous and satisfied smile! So, the whole world in turmoil is "busy"; the giants of various countries are "busy" with how to make their regimes more centralized and violent; diplomats are "busy" with intrigue, scheming, and colluding with each other; the "valve" characters of the army, navy, and air force are "busy" with expanding their budgets and rushing to build warships, airplanes, and tanks; Buddhist laymen and "children of God" are "busy" with "praying for peace" as in the old example of the European war. In this tense atmosphere where everyone is "busy," only the old black shirt leader Mussolini and the new brown shirt leader Hitler are, in addition to being "busy" with everything that imperialists should be "busy" with, even more "busy" with encouraging the "Chichi Yuanyuan" [common people] of their respective countries to process and rush to build the second generation of little citizens or little fascists. "Bearing, gathering, teaching, and training," "seeing the micro and knowing the far," we really cannot but admire the abilities of these two black and brown "star lords," who are indeed different from ordinary people.

On the "Wedding Festival" of October 30, Mussolini presented gifts to 2,000 married couples, and also gave a set of new clothes to the babies who participated in the baptism ceremony on that day: The Prime Minister also gave a birthday speech, saying that 1934 will become a "four-year" for single men, that is, the government will levy taxes on those who do not marry.

Hitler has examined the physique of 1.5 million young men and women in Germany in the past three months, and like Mussolini, he encourages marriage. According to the application of the married, the government can lend each married couple 600 marks. According to Reuters on November 22, there are already 10,000 people in Berlin who have applied for loans at the registration office.

The significance of this "new strategy" of rewarding sexual intercourse and spreading seeds is very obvious. First, it shows that the imperialists are determined to go to war. In order to prepare for the terrible sacrifices of killing everywhere and rivers of blood, the strong men who are prepared to go to the front line to "fight for the motherland" must have the need to spread seeds and rush to build "reserve cannon fodder." Second, it shows the terrible destructive power of modern war on mankind and all civilized achievements. The European war, which lasted for four years of indiscriminate killing and chopping, resulted in "only" the creation of several tombs that together accommodated more than 2 million soldiers as "unknown heroes." However, now, after more than ten years of "continuous improvement" in killing technology, the infinite development of air force power, and the greater application of chemistry to war, the destructive power of war has increased several times compared to the European war, making major cities such as London, New York, and Tokyo in danger of being turned into ruins at any time under the attack of the enemy's air force. Under this terrible war race of "digging their own graves," how can imperialists, who are certainly no less clever than you and me, not worry about the "extinction" or "reduced production" of "cannon fodder" and "reserve army of industry" in the future - so Mussolini and Hitler's reward for "manufacturing little citizens" is really based on the actual needs of war mania, not only for the sake of "improving the race" or "multiplying the population," nor just for solving the "sexual desire problem" for his disciples and grandchildren,

Why did the wooden clogs "friends" who rushed to the forefront of the war give up this fashionable game of "rewarding people"? The reason is very simple: First, the population growth rate in Japan was originally higher than in Italy and Germany, so there is no need for "processing and rushing to build"; second, after cutting off Manchuria, they have gained more than 10 million "cannon fodder" (excluding "women"), which they do not need to manufacture themselves. Why not "generously" use the "heads" of others in the war?

Imperialism is "processing and manufacturing people" for the sake of mass slaughter, while our country is advocating "national martial arts" in order to "resist." Comparing the two, I see that the heads of many compatriots have been "reserved" to dance wildly in the burning Pacific fire! Alas! What else can I say!

Novel

Shanghai (12)

— Zhang Lao San

I briefly described the changes this time, and I have decided to leave my family. Based on the lessons we have learned, we will restore our Zhengyi Society. Although our younger brother is a fifteen-year-old child, he has firm self-confidence. If he cannot help our society, he will not destroy it. "Gao Fei, do you allow my younger brother to join?" I stared at Gao Fei, while seeking the opinions of the entire table.

"I agree, two love experts!" Little Huang was the first to jump up again.

Twenty, you don't have a wife yet.

When we came out of the restaurant, it was already nine o'clock. Gao Fei said, why don't you stay at the society tonight? Little Huang, Chongqing, and Xiaofeng are all at the society, so Little Huang won't shout for three missing one.

A group of people laughed and talked. The spring breeze on Avenue Joffre, intoxicating, blew on our faces. My heart fluttered, as if I was thrown into the arms of a lover. Thinking carefully about what had happened in the past two days, the crisp footsteps echoed as we stepped on the sidewalk.

At the Rue Luber intersection, everyone parted ways. The four of us walked south. Perhaps joy occupied everyone's hearts, and we all walked slowly, with our long, thin shadows dappling. Only Little Huang was jumping and walking, and the shadow of the person on the ground was like a short winter melon. Xiaofeng joked with him:

"Little Huang, mahjong tonight?"

"Okay! Okay!" He forgot he was running. "It's really hard to find a partner. Once they have a wife, they all want to go home to sleep."

"You don't have a wife yet?" I asked.

Little Huang glanced at me and shook his head, seeming to feel sad. Little Huang is a famous optimist in our society, but talking about wives makes him sad. He said himself, love is not known to be the real thing, I have not met a woman who loves me! From then on, I made fun of him as a topic, and he returned the nickname "love expert."

When we arrived at the society on Route Lafayette, Little Huang lay down on the bed. Chongqing and Xiaofeng deliberately turned the mahjong tiles over on the table and played with them. Little Huang pouted and covered his head with a quilt, and we laughed together.

Two hours later, they were all fast asleep. The surroundings were as quiet as death, with the occasional horn sound of a speeding car. I looked at the ceiling, tossing and turning, unable to fall asleep. Helplessly, I sat up and wrote a letter to Sister Min, telling her about today's events: how my uncle prevaricated me, my cousin's situation, my younger brother's letter, and finally meeting old friends from the past. I wrote in a jumbled manner, filling three sheets of letter paper. I lit a cigarette and read it again, but it seemed unsatisfactory. Why tell her so much? Suddenly, Little Huang laughed. I thought he had seen my situation, but he turned over and fell asleep again. He probably had a dream about a woman? I couldn't help but smile at the letter paper myself, struck a match, and folded the three sheets of letter paper and burned them. I picked up the pen again and wrote simply.

Amateur Mailbox

Flower Fallen into the Privy

To the Esteemed Editor:

When I was four years old, due to the pressure of money, my parents sold me to someone for more than a hundred yuan. At first, I inevitably cried and made a fuss, but after two or three months, I gradually got used to it. Who knew that when I turned fourteen, my foster mother forced me into prostitution. Although I knew this was a vile thing, I finally succumbed to this wretched path to avoid the pain of being beaten and scolded. Alas! Can my fate still be imagined? Who knew that this year, my foster mother, having obtained more than a thousand yuan, married me off to a forty-something civil servant who already has a wife. Sir—please think about it! Would an eighteen-year-old girl willingly marry him? But, unable to withstand the coercion, I reluctantly stamped the marriage certificate during a simple wedding ceremony. In the latter half of my time as a prostitute, I met a young student, whose character, temperament, and learning were all excellent, not to mention his feelings. He once tried to commit suicide because his family prevented him from marrying me. Now he has obtained a decent job, is no longer bound by his family's finances, and can officially marry me. But what about me? I am already a married woman. If I don't divorce my current husband, my lover and I will never become a couple. But what are the divorce procedures? Should I file a lawsuit? What are the grounds? Can I actually get divorced? This matter truly puts me in a dilemma. Sir, you are the compass of society. Please answer these questions. Respectfully wishing you good health.

Respectfully,

Sun Meixian

× × × × ×

Editor's Note: If Ms. Sun files a lawsuit with the court to sever her relationship with her current husband, the other party will definitely not strongly resist. Firstly, because he is a married man, to avoid the crime of bigamy, your relationship is merely that of a husband and concubine. The binding force of this type of relationship is far less close than that of a married couple in the eyes of the law; it can be kept if agreeable, or abandoned if not. Secondly, because he is a civil servant, openly taking a concubine will undoubtedly affect his future. Thirdly, although you stamped the marriage certificate, judging from the common psychology that an eighteen-year-old girl would never willingly marry a man over forty, no one would doubt that this matter was coerced.

However, your husband may suspect that you and your foster mother are engaged in fraudulent behavior and file a counterclaim. But your foster mother will be responsible for this. Even if you received a small share of the more than a thousand yuan she took, the amount would not be much; the majority would naturally be enjoyed by your foster mother. She spent more than a hundred yuan to buy you, endured ten years of simple meals, used you as a cash cow for four years, and finally acted without conscience, ruining your life. It would be good for her to receive some retribution, as a warning to others.

Market News

Aviation Little Series is About to be Published

Since the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, the public has gradually realized the importance of aviation. The government is doing its best to promote it, and the people are donating funds to purchase aircraft. Even young children are saving their candy money for this purpose. It is now reported that the Aviation Administration has specially compiled and published a variety of Aviation Little Series for children's education, with one issue every week. The content is divided into stories, flight, air defense, travelogues, warfare, anecdotes, maxims, anecdotes, speeches, etc., with colorful covers and photographic illustrations. The text is simple and fluent, and the printing is exquisite and beautiful, making it very suitable for children to read. The cost is kept low, and special discounts are offered for long-term subscriptions. All parents who love their children should subscribe for a long term, it is said.

Aviation Yearbook Will Soon be Completed

It has been more than twenty years since aviation was established in our country. Due to political changes in the past, there has been little progress. Since the national government established its capital in Nanjing and the political system was unified, the aviation industry has also flourished. Although it is not enough to compare with other countries, fortunately it has taken on a basic form. If the public's assistance is effective, the future will be bright. Since Mr. Xu Peigen has been the head of the Aviation Administration, he has made many achievements in promoting aviation, and he is particularly enthusiastic about popularizing aviation education. In addition to the Aviation Magazine and Aviation Bulletin issued by the Administration, which have already become popular for a while, the China Aviation Yearbook is also being compiled, totaling several chapters and 300,000 words. It is reported that the manuscript can be completed and printed within the year.

Self-Employment Introduction

A certain gentleman, a graduate of the preparatory course of Aurora University, is proficient in Chinese and French, has a slight understanding of English, and seeks a suitable occupation, salary not counted. Those interested please write to Mr. Wu Mingjun at Aurora University.
